Sustainability Report
2023
 056
Risk Description:
A vibrant market for AI applications has emerged in recent years 
due to AI adoption by industries, and the development of the 
AI industry. IDC statistics indicated that the total value of the 
global AI market including income from software, hardware, and 
services will surpass US$500 billion in 2023.
The Possible Impact on The Company:
That is why the Company has focused on developments relating 
to 5G and AI PC industry trends in recent years. However, the 
shortage of professionals and the increasing demand for AI and 
5G applications across industries has created fierce competition 
in human resources such as recruitment failure risks. According 
to government statistics, over 55% of companies report a 
shortage of AI-related talents. Trends such as talent competition 
have led to an imbalance between the demand and the available 
supply for AI and 5G professionals in emerging technologies. 
This shortage crisis not only result in uncertainty in the human 
capital but also create a gap in human resources that will 
intensify the competition for talent in products research and 
innovation such as 5G Small Cell, 5G communication businesses, 
and AI PCs. 
At the same time, Taiwan is however facing a loss of continuity in 
human resources due to an aging population and declining birth 
rate. Government statistics suggest that the working population 
in Taiwan will decline to 67% in 2030. The Company is also 
faced with the prospect of many employees reaching retirement 
age. Our remuneration may not be sufficient to compete with 
international enterprises and competitors, leading to risk of 
difficulty with recruiting and retaining talent in emerging 
technologies.
The Company Plans to Adopt the Following Response 
Measures: 
To recruit, attract, and retain quality talent, the Company uses 
video streaming platforms, social media and other channels to 
share our benefits. We have also designed holistic development/
retention mechanisms as well as a vision for learning and 
development to boost our appeal to the younger generation.
Talent Shortage Risk Due to Declining Birth Rate and Emerging Industry Trends 
03.4.4 Identification of Emerging Risks

NHI and Social Insurance Insolvency Creates Risk of Failure for Diversification
::: Introduction to the Report
::: 2023 Sustainability Accolades

Risk Description: 
The Company currently invests in three main areas of smart 
healthcare. The first is medical devices including ultrasound 
inhalers, blood sugar meters and other hardware; the second is 
cell therapy, stem cells, and CAR-T cell therapy. The third is day 
care and long-term care services. The National Health Insurance 
(NHI) system in Taiwan was implemented in 1995. NHI is 
considered an example of a successful social insurance scheme 
that provides medical protection and high-quality health 
services for the whole population. NHI has been in serious 
financial crisis in recent years, however. It is expected to end 
up in the red in 2024 and exhaust its preparatory fund by 2030. 
If this should happen, it will lead to risks such as government 
cuts on health expenditure including reduced subsidies for new 
medical technologies, medical devices, and drugs, lower market 
demand, reduced income, as well as obstacles to R&D and 
innovation.
The Possible Impact on The Company: 
Compal plans to continue developing and investing in the 
medtech, medical application technology, and bio-technology 
industries in the future. The radio frequency ablation system 
that recently reached the market for example has already 
approved for NHI coverage under the existing special materials 
code by the Ministry of Health and Welfare. The approval took 
effect on September 1, 2023, so the NHI insolvency crisis may 
have the following impacts on Compal: 
Reduced income and profits for the Company: NHI 
insolvency may lead to reduction in health expenditures, 
which in turn reduces public demand for medical products 
and services.
R&D and investment constraints: R&D activities of 
biotechnology companies may face constraints due to 
their depending on funding from the government or other 
payment institutions. If the government cuts spending on 
medical research, or a reduction in the Company’s income 
results in cuts to R&D budgets, the innovation capacity of 
the Company may be affected.
Increased uncertainty in the market: NHI insolvency may 
lead to increased uncertainty in the market including 
changes in medical costs, policy adjustments, and shifts in 
market competition.

3.
3.
The Company Plans to Adopt the Following Response 
Measures: 
The Company is collaborating with the New Taipei 
City Government on the Ruifang Hospital BOT project. 
Partnering with the government on expanding fields for 
actual application of medical products will help ensure the 
sustainability of the industry.
The Company is investing in other health-related industries 
as well as building overseas plants and exporting products 
overseas to increase our sources of income.
The Company is also expanding beyond remote medical 
devices and long-term care into animal-related medical 
products as well.

Compal’s operating locations across the world collaborates 
with local government on community relationship management 
in a manner that conforms to stakeholder expectations; our 
operating locations support local initiatives on health cities to 
uphold the philosophy of sustainability.
The following activities are aimed at enhancing social welfare 
and improving our corporate image so that Compal can become 
a respected world-class enterprise: 
Schools and Talent Cultivation
Strengthening of industry-university collaboration by helping 
cooperative education students obtain work-related knowledge 
and experience at school. The medium and long-term benefits 
include the cultivation of future management talent and 
promotion of local prosperity. At the same time, Compal also 
offers job openings for alternative military service to provide 
cooperative education or other students with a direct transition 
to the workforce upon graduation.
Hospitals and Healthcare
Compal Headquarters established the”Sunshine Vitality 
Clinic”and retained physicians with extensive clinical experience 
to provide holistic physical and mental healthcare to employees, 
local residents, and office workers. We hope to combine the 
clinic with medical technology to create a new model for smart 
healthcare.
At the same time, Compal, Tainan City Government and 
Taiwan Genkimura (a subsidiary of the Japanese Genki 
Group) partnered to set up the Long-term Care Center with 
Multiple Levels of Long-term Care and Continuous Care 
Environment.”Japanese-style boutique care techniques and 
Compal smart technology were introduced with “Healthcare, 
Long-term Care, Education”as the core pillars to support 
local seniors. The initiative is aimed at realizing a “Long-Life, 
Symbiotic, Harmonious Society”and lay the foundations for 
Compal iCare.
Compal has also signed a BOT+BTO contract for New Taipei 
City’s Ruifang District Medical and Long-term Care Facilities 
Building. The project is scheduled for completion in 2026. Once 
complete, it will improve medical capabilities in the community 
and demonstrate Compal’s commitment to giving back to 
society.
Government Agencies and Civic Responsibility
Compal cooperates with government polices (Tax Bureau, 
Customs, MOEA, Social Welfare Bureau etc.) on improving 
the local community environment so that they can become 
safe, law-abiding, clean, and environmentally friendly, 
sustainability communities. Regular fire drills (fire prevention, 
water prevention, quake prevention, ice prevention) are 
regularly conducted in accordance with the disaster prevention 
guidelines defined by government agencies (police, fire 
department etc.). We also formulate relevant SOPs and set 
emergency response teams. These not only comply with 
statutory requirements but also enhance peace of mind in local 
communities, and protect the safety of our employees and 
company assets.
Maintaining Harmony with Borough Offices, Building 
Management Committees and Residents
Waste Disposal and Environmental Protection
We practice proactive management of waste contractors to 
ensure that all waste produced by the Company are disposed in 
accordance with environmental regulations. E-waste that may 
pose a hazard to the environment are treated with particular 
care to prevent damage to our business reputation as well as 
safeguard the right to a healthy life among local residents.

03.5	
Compliance, Ethical Management and Anti-Corruption
03.5.1	 Ethical Management and Anti-Corruption
 060
1.	 To strengthen business integrity standards Compal, 
the Company has always maintained a zero-tolerance 
approach to corruption and bribery to ensure effective 
response to risks relating to conflicts of interest. A Compal 
ethical management and anti-corruption system has been 
established using the ISO 37001 international standard on 
anti-bribery management systems to meet the expectations 
of international organizations on transparency and 
disclosure assessments, and to comply with the regulations 
and expectations of the competent authorities.
2.	 The ethical management and anti-corruption management 
team periodically strengthens internal management and 
audit procedures in line with best practice at international 
benchmark companies, the US Foreign Corrupt Practices Act 
(FCPA), and the UK Bribery Act (UKBA) of 2010. Our efforts 
have laid down a solid foundation for our globalization 
strategy and quest to become a leading international 
enterprise.

The anti-corruption and anti-bribery management system/
procedures were jointly developed and implemented by the 
governance body (Board of Directors) and management body 
(managers at all levels managed by President) based on the 
organizational structure and business scale of Compal, as well 
as the international political-economic situation.
The primary mission is to ensure that “Accountability”is 
embedded in the consciousness of all employees. 
Whistleblower safeguards are in place so that whistle blowers 
that provide evidence of corruption and bribery do not have to 
fear retribution or revenge. Continued to optimize the 3 Lines 
of Defense for risk management and internal audit & control 
system while also refining the reporting and whistleblower 
systems.
Business partners are thoroughly assessed on potential 
corruption and bribery risks based on the formative factors of 
the Fraud Triangle. The seven following initiatives were also 
implemented to ensure the effectiveness of the Company’s risk 
management and monitoring mechanisms!
Unwavering support and commitment from the Board of 
Directors and management team.
Development plans with comprehensive supervision and 
process controls that integrate the 3 Lines of Defense in risk 
management.
Clear and up to date management regulations on anti-
corruption policy and ethical management.
Annual risk assessments, measurements and responses for 
assurance of internal audits and retention of audit trails.
Joint promotion of anti-corruption and anti-bribery with 
business partners.
Company-wide employee training and communication as 
well as the establishment of a management culture with 
clearly defined rewards and punishments.
Establish and publicize the reporting process with periodic 
management reviews and supervision.

2023
 062
I. Work flow for processing of fraud and 
corruption complaints
1)	 Clear principles and division of labor 
have been established for the processing of 
corruption and fraud complaints by the Auditing 
Office.
2)	 Once a fraud or corruption complaint is 
received by the Auditing Office, the contents 
should be analyzed and the provided 
information should be put on record.
3)	 The reliability of the complaint should be 
assessed to prevent malicious accusations or 
vexatious complaints. If the complaint can 
be substantiated and the provided evidence 
can be verified, a task force is set up after the 
assessment by the Auditing Office to conduct an 
investigation.
4)	 Once a complaint has been accepted, the 
case should be studied and the relevant units 
should be consulted. A review based on external 
laws and internal operating rules should be 
planned. An investigation may commence with 
the approval of the authorized supervisor. 
The review may involve system audits, 
correspondence, review of applicable forms and 
receipts, interviews, consultations, and on-site 
inspections.
5)	 The Auditing Office maintain an accurate 
and complete record of complaints. The case 
should be carefully handled in accordance 
with the principles of confidentiality, legality, 
reasonableness, swiftness, and effective closure.
II. Work flow for protection of complainants 
and whistleblowers
1)	 Make sure that the whistleblower is provided 
with safeguards on compensation, personal 
safety, and mental security. The reporting 
of illegal activities is to be encouraged to 
strengthen the enforcement of risk management 
and supervision by the Company, effectively 
promote a culture of integrity at Compal, and 
ensure the sustainability of the enterprise.
2)	 Complainants or whistleblowers that make 
use of the complaints channels should be 
offered all possible protection. Complainants 
should have nothing in fear for reporting 
illegal activities such as bribery, corruption, 
blackmail, or extortion. The lawful interest of 
all those involved should be protected. Compal 
will launch an investigation if it any unit or 
individual should engage in retribution against 
a complainant or whistleblower after the fact. 
Disciplinary action will be taken against those 
responsible if the complaint is found to be true. 
Those who violate the law should be referred to 
law enforcement.
3)	 The complainant can make anonymous 
reports to provide all the relevant facts including 
the subject of their complaint’s name, unit, 
position, address, the name of the unit they are 
filing a complaint against, as well as the facts, 
clues, or evidence of the improper conduct. 
The Auditing Office should maintain the 
confidentiality of the complaints they receive. 
If a complaint is made in person, it should be 
conducted in a confidential location and the 
interview recorded by dedicated personnel. Only 
authorized personnel may attend the interview 
and ask questions.
4)	 If an employee is aware of the complainant 
or whistleblower’s identity due to their position 
or the nature of their work, they must not 
leak any identifying information related to the 
complainant. Information that can be used to 
identify the complainant, their written complaint 
and interview records, or the evidence they 
provided should all be encrypted for protection. 
Access should also be restricted with no 
unauthorized copying of extracts or duplication.
5)	 The information provided by the 
complainant should be used with care during 
the investigation. The information provided 
by the complainant should be used cautiously 
and must not be revealed at random to keep 
the subject of the complaint from guessing 
the identity of the complainant. No identifying 
information related to the complainant and the 
contents/evidence of their complainant may 
be revealed or published before the end of 
investigations.
6)	 Once the investigation is complete, 
information that can be used to identify the 
complainant as well as the written complaint, 
interview records or evidence should be stored 
separately from the investigation files unless 
absolutely necessary.
7)	 If a complainant is subjected to improper 
treatment due to making a complaint, the 
Compal Group should ask the competent unit 
to provide corrective action, restoration, or 
compensation. If a complainant is being publicly 
recognized then identifying information may not 
be released without the complainant’s consent.
Under the globalization strategy adopted by 
Compal, the development and supervision of 
anti-corruption/anti-bribery tasks already take 
the regulatory requirements of each country 
into account for compliance. The Board of 
Directors has also directed the Auditing Office 
to monitor the “design”and “execution”aspects 
of internal control procedures. The Board 
is briefed on the validity of the system at 
least once a year to ensure the continued 
improvement of related processes.
All employees, partners and stakeholders of 
the Compal Group should use the grievances 
channel to contact the Group if they discover 
any evidence on violation of anti-corruption 
policy and management regulations relating to 
ethical management. Compal Group promises 
to handle all cases in the strictest confidence. 
The Group also promises to do everything 
in its power to protect the complainant from 
retribution.
A variety of complaint channels has been 
established by the Company to listen to 
feedback from stakeholders. The whistleblower 
complaints mailbox and telephone number are 
already published on our corporate website, 
Compal Procurement System (CPS), and the 
Compal ESG webpage.
Complaints mailbox: ethics@compal.com
Complaints number: (02) 8797-8599 #16055

 063
 A corruption risk assessment of all global operating 
locations are conducted by Compal at least once a year. On-
site or written assessment is conducted depending on the 
operating risk and materiality.
Covered locations include: Taiwan Headquarters, China, 
Vietnam, North America, Central and South Americas, and 
Europe. Coverage over the last two years both reached 100%.
Note: CaSA: Central and South Americas
The Company has established a complaints mailbox and 
hotline (02) 8797-8599 #16055 for stakeholders to report 
or file a dispute when they see any unethical behavior by 
employees. Annual inspections of ethical management 
are also conducted by the Auditing Office with the results 
described below:
No employees were disciplined for violation of the Ethical 
Corporate Management Best Practice Principles in 2023.
Education and training on ethical management topics are 
periodically hosted by the Company. In 2023, the classes 
were taken 8,840 times and total duration of 9,567 hours. 
Sampling confirmed that all students conducted the required 
hours of training and passed the course.
Suppliers that the Company traded with in 2023 were 
required to sign the Commitment to the RBA Code of 
Conduct or self-assessment. Signatures were provided by 
924 out of 937 suppliers. The signing rate is currently 99%.
An annual risk assessment is conducted by Compal based 
on the three risk factors of operating risk, compliance, 
and internal controls. An annual management plan is also 
formulated.
The Auditing Office takes the risk factors for unethical 
conduct into account when formulating the annual audit 
plan. These are implemented throughout the overall 
assessment and a review was conducted based on the 
findings of the assessment.
The analysis and response strategies for material corruption 
risks identified through risk assessment have already been 
confirmed by a Board of Directors meeting on March 12, 
2024. All 15 directors in attendance agreed that the risk 
assessment, internal control management and response 
strategies completed by the Company were sufficient to 
effectively counter material corruption and fraud risks.

(I). 2023 Accomplishments
(1) Ethical management training for Board members
The Company encourages and assists directors with enhancing their understanding of the ethical 
management philosophy and management skills. Kinpo Group Management Consultant Company, a 
Group affiliate, was commissioned to hold the courses required by law. Related courses were also held 
by external professional bodies. Board members had completed 107 hours of continuing education as of 
December 31, 2023.

 067
Disciplinary regulations were established for compliance with 
the Code of Conduct and linked to remuneration. Where 
employee behavior violated the Code of Conduct, and resulting 
in significant risk events such as poor strategic judgment, 
or internal personnel corruption, which severely affect the 
company’s reputation or profitability, disciplinary action will be 
taken including termination of employment in serious cases.
Regularly review and evaluate the corporate code of conduct 
to identify the areas for improvement, ensuring its relevance, 
effectiveness, and up-to-date. Certification of compliance 
execution is taken for corrective measures to prevent 
recurrence, including violation reporting, investigations, tracking 
and evaluating internal control system, etc. All these procedures 
are verified by third-party.
There was no record of major violations at Compal in 2023 
(involving fines/sanctions of more than NT$1 million, or 
reported in the media).

CHAPTER

To protect confidential company and customer information, Compal passed ISO 27001 Information Security 
inspection in 2005 and was awarded “ISO 27001”certification by BSI. Since then, the scope of certification 
has been expanded and the Company has been conducting regular follow-ups twice every year and a 
review audit once every three years. Internal auditing are including the NIST CSF, ISO/IEC 27001: 2022 and 
TISAX standards; external third-party audits are based on the ISO/IEC 27001: 2022 standards as well as 
the information security requirements of our customers. The scope of verification covers R&D activities of 
portable computer, all-in-one PC, automotive electronic product, server product, mobile device product, IT 
group, smart device business group-IT division, and IT division at four factories in Kunshan. All of the above 
information security audits are aimed at ensuring proper enforcement of information security standards and 
continued validity of ISO/IEC 27001 certification by the Company.
Sustainability Report
2023
03.6 Privacy and Information Security
 068
ISO 27001 Information Security Management System
Information Security Policy and Organization
Compal conducts management review meetings twice a year 
to enforce the requirements of the ISO 27001 information 
management system. Information security policy was defined 
as the highest guiding principle to maintain our competitive 
advantage, protect our valuable intellectual property, as well as 
ensure that proper safeguards are in place for the information 
and information systems involved in product operations. 
The statement of information security is “ensure business 
continuity and enhance customer satisfaction”. Compal adheres 
absolutely to the privacy policy and prohibits the secondary 
use of customer data. We have confirmed that there has 
been no secondary use in actual practice (0%). There were 
no substantiated complaints on invasion of customer privacy 
or loss of customer information in the past three years. The 
Compal information security policy is as follows: 
Implement risk assessment of information assets.
Maintain the confidentiality, integrity and availability of critical 
information assets.
Continuously improve the information security system through 
the Plan-Do-Check-Act (PDCA) management cycle.
Firmly comply with customer contracts to protect customer 
information security.
Follow and comply with relevant government information 
security regulations.
Employees and contractors fully participate in the process.

Information Security Committee    
The Information Security Committee is the coordination and 
execution organization for Compal’s information security-
related operations and activities. It has a chairman and a deputy 
chairman, and may set up a number of members according to 
management needs, with the head of each department and 
above as ex-officio members. It also has an executive secretary 
responsible for administrative affairs. Under the Information 
Security Committee, there is an Information Security Execution 
Team, which is composed of members from the Information 
Security Team of the Information Department to handle the 
establishment, promotion, maintenance, audit and training 
of information security. The Information Security Committee 
reports the implementation status to the Board meeting once a 
year. When necessary, the Information Security Committee may 
invite external information security consultants to attend the 
Board meeting for consultation.
Compal’s Information Security Committee coordinates and 
studies information security policies, objectives and resource 
scheduling, and holds management review meetings twice a 
year to ensure the continued applicability, appropriateness and 
effectiveness of the ISMS (Information Security Management 
System), and maintain operational information security and 
compliance with national laws and the requirements of 
competent authorities for information security control. Define 
the scope of the information security management system, 
perform risk assessment and risk management tasks, determine 
acceptable risk levels, negotiate duties and responsibilities in 
information security-related operations, and coordinate various 
control measures and processing procedures for information 
security. Promote information security policies and information 
security management concepts, and promote corporate 
information security education and training.

Continued Maintenance of Information Security
Enhance Network Security
Enhance Sharing of Information Security 
Intelligence
Compal measures six major information security objectives 
on a monthly basis, and monitors the measures of 
information security management control.
The identification of internal external issues with the 
information security management is conducted every 
six months to establish stakeholder expectations of the 
information security management system (including 
customer requirements on information security).
A backup and recovery test is conducted every six months 
and a BCP recovery drill is conducted every year to ensure 
the effectiveness of the BCP plan and compliance with the 
system recovery goal.
Information security incident response drills are conducted 
every year so that information security incidents can be 
contained and threats resolved as quickly as possible to 
reduce the scope and degree of impact.
Social engineering drills & information security guidance are 
conducted every quarter, while education training conducted 
every year to enhance employee information security 
awareness.
To detect network and system vulnerabilities, vulnerability 
scans are periodically conducted and professional third-
parties commissioned to carry out network and system 
penetration tests every year to verify the effectiveness and 
performance of information security defenses.
Internal/external audits are conducted on a regular basis 
along with continuous improvement.
Risk assessment is carried out on a regular basis and risk 
assessments conducted based on asset value and business 
processes. Risk control measures are then carried out for 
areas assessed to be of high risk.
Compal continues to enhance information security control 
requirements and strengthen the Company’s password policy, 
and has adjusted the non-reusability of the previous three 
password setting to ten. Strengthen the Company’s account 
identity authentication mechanism and introduce two-factor 
authentication to enhance the security of remote login to 
internal resources and prevent illegal users from accessing 
company resources or customer information. Establishment of 
MDR threat detection, anomaly analysis and event response 
to protect against information security threats. Access to 
sensitive information is controlled by account permissions. 
The login password shall be regularly changed in accordance 
with the Company’s password policy. Continue to examine the 
Company’s network security plan and ensure the compliance 
of all devices connected to the corporate network. Compal 
began carrying third-party cybersecurity assessment in 2020. 
According to the Security Scorecard for industry and scale, 
Compal scored an average of 94 in 2023. This was higher than 
the global average for manufacturing companies.
To improve our ability to report and respond to information 
security incidents, Compal applied for membership of the 
Taiwan Computer Emergency Response Team/Coordination 
Center (TWCERT/CC) in 2022 in accordance with the “Guide to 
Information Security Management for Public Companies”issued 
by the government.

Strategic Objectives
Sustainability Report

03.7 Responsible Investment
 071
By leveraging its core competence, Compal has planned 
new strategies for growth given the three major trends of 
global economic power transition, demographic changes 
and acceleration in technological advancement. Apart 
from continuing to actively strengthen vertical integration 
in the supply chain, the Company will also be applying its 
ICT experiences and advantages to other domains such as 
industrial computer, industry/service automation, IoT related 
sectors, smart medicine sector, biotech sector and so forth.
Particular emphasis was placed on the smart medicine 
industry. Compal launched our next-generation industry 
strategy in 2015 targeting the rapid increase in medical 
expenditure due to an aging population. The software and 
hardware technologies accumulated by Compal in the ICT 
industry would be integrated with Taiwan’s advantage in 
medical talent and resources. In addition to the smart health 
care and health care platform system developed in-house by 
Compal (SMT, HMT, Software Team), a number of investments 
have also served to flesh out Compal’s smart medicine 
strategy. A medical industry supply chain that encompasses 
everything from biotechnology, pharmaceuticals, medical 
devices, medical services, to biometric information is now 
gradually taking shape. In the future, we have set our sights 
on smart hospitals and hospital information management 
systems. The introduction of medical big data will help realize 
our dream of “precision medicine.”
In 2021,Compal successfully bid for surface rights to site 
T16 at Beitou-Shilin Technology Park with the Taipei City 
Government. The site will become a smart campus for Compal 
headquarters. Once Compal becomes the tenant here, T16 
will be forged into a transnational smart campus based 
around the five axes of smart economy, smart health, smart 
transportation, smart environment, and smart buildings. 
Domestic and overseas talent will also be recruited to 
create more job opportunities. At the same time, Compal 
is continuing to move forward on our smart medicine 
strategy. All regions are treated equally though we try to 
inject more resources into remote rural regions. The “New 
Taipei City Ruifang Senior Care Facility BOT + BTO”investment 
program”was subsequently signed with the Taipei City 
Department of Health in 2022 with completion scheduled 
for 2026. The BOT project will see Compal bring about 
the tight-knit integration of emergency medical services, 
community healthcare and long-term care resources. A host 
of technologies and service models such as tele-medicine, 
medical IoT, and long-term care systems will be introduced 
in the future. A composite healthcare approach that 
incorporates charity resources will be established to solving 
the shortage of long-term care resources. Investment was 
primarily aimed at creating more value for the local economy 
embracing the social philosophy of “full employment”and 
“aged in place”. Additionally, Compal continued to increase 
our investment in Kinpo Group Headquarters Asset 
Development Corporation and Compal Ruifang Health Assets 
Development Corporation to a tune of NT$3.7 billion in 2023. 
Compal also increased our investment in existing investees 
in 2023. These included further investments in Cal-Comp 
Electronics (Thailand) Pub Co., Ltd. and AcBel Polytech Inc. 
based on strategic business considerations to boost Group 
synergy. During the course of 2023,new Compal investments 
included mainly the following: 
Kinpo&Compal Group Assets Development Corporation
In 2021,Compal successfully bid for surface rights in BSTP 
put up for tender by the Taipei City Government to support 
the sustainable development of the Kinpo Group and plans 
for business headquarters. The Kinpo Headquarters Asset 
Development Corp. was therefore formed to handle the 
construction, operation, tendering, leasing, and property 
management of the future Kinpo Headquarters.
Compal Ruifang Health Assets Development Corporation
Mainly responsible for the construction of “Ruifang 
Hospital”and the operation of the long-term care facility.
Cal-Comp Electronics (Thailand) Pub Co., Ltd.
Electronics Manufacturing Services (EMS)
AcBel Polytech Inc.
Business portfolio consists of R&D, production and sale of 
“Power Supply Units”
Pharmaceuticals
Medical Services
 Medical Equipment
Electro-Mechanical 
Information
Biotechnology

CHAPTER

Compal’s Investment Procedure
Future Investment Plans
Sustainability Report
2023
 072
Prudent and Cautious Assessment Prior to Investment
Careful and Meticulous Management after Investment
Select suitable industries in accordance with the 
aforementioned strategies.
Assess key factors such as the trends of sector 
development, market supply and demand, status of 
competition and so forth.
Assess potential target’s core competence and 
competitiveness by looking at indicators such as 
technological capabilities, talents, finances and so 
forth.
Perform due diligence on the target company through 
on-site visits and investigation of the company’s 
reputation.
Carry out the investment in accordance with the 
Company’s Guidelines for Handling Acquisition and 
Disposal of Assets.
Operations of the investment (once the investment 
has been finalized), Compal shall carry out relevant 
planning for the new subsidiary/reinvestment in which 
the Company has specific influence over, including: 
director/supervisor planning, management team audit, 
CPA planning, review of employee incentive program 
after its formulation, review of charter of incorporation/
key procedures as required by pertinent regulations after 
their formulation, review of approval authorities and 
relevant procedures pertaining to said authorities after 
establishment and so forth.
Analyze and review relevant management report and 
outcome of management review meeting as carried out 
by the subsidiary/reinvestment in which the Company has 
specific influence over.
Compal’s investment management unit shall refer to 
pertinent procedures and regulations by monitoring and 
watching out for any warning signs in the operation of 
subsidiaries/reinvestments; the unit shall also routinely 
take part in the meetings and visit various subsidiaries, 
affiliates and reinvestments to collect relevant reports 
on governance, interviews, meeting records, etc for 
approval and archival. We also collaborate with finance 
and accounting departments to review financial 
and accounting principles, and to devise investment 
withdrawal plans where appropriate.
Compal follows the principle of steady operation and always 
focuses on our core business. We only expand on the foundation 
of our existing businesses. In addition to growing our core 
businesses, we also make vertical business integrations where 
appropriate and expand horizontally into related business 
activities. Compal, Kinpo and its affiliates will proceed with 
the aforementioned expansion based on the consideration 
of whether the expansion can strengthen the Group’s 
advantage and assessment of reasonable risks. Investments 
followed the above principles and were directed in the three 
basic directions shown on the left. In all three investment 
directions, sustainability investment was made the prerequisite 
by incorporating ESG assessment into investment decisions. 
Financial factors were also taken into account to seek better 
returns and risk control. In practice, apart from achieving internal 
growth under the existing business framework, we also accept 
the possibility of mergers, acquisitions, joint ventures, and 
bilateral or multi-lateral collaborations.

4.1.1 Environment Sustainability Management
Sustainability Report
2023
04.1 Sustainable Environment and Commitment
 074
Although Compal does not belong to high-energy-consumption 
or high-water-consumption industries, we remain committed 
to monitoring the negative environmental impacts of our 
operations and actively improving the efficiency of energy, 
water use, reducing the waste of various resources, lowering 
emissions of waste and pollutants to achieve the goal of 
environmental sustainability. The company has established 
a series of short-term goals and strategies, including a 1% 
reduction in electricity, water usage, and waste intensity 
compared to the previous year. These goals are implemented 
through regular tracking and verification to ensure effective 
environmental performance management. Moreover, to 
thoroughly implement Compal’s environmental sustainability 
management philosophy from top to bottom and continuously 
reduce the consumption of various resources and optimize their 
usage efficiency, we regularly conduct educational training. This 
helps communicate our environmental management objectives 
to all employees, enhancing their awareness of energy 
conservation, water conservation, waste reduction, and green 
product design and manufacturing, thereby realizing various 
action plans for environmental sustainability management.
We actively study the environmental impacts of the product 
life cycle and introduce the circular economy concept during 
the product design phase. Compal strives to reduce the 
environmental impact of our products. We also promote the 
research and development of energy-efficiency and eco-friendly 
products. These targets and strategies are proposed by each 
functional team to the Sustainability Committee. Once they are 
approved by the Chair of the Sustainability Committee and Chief 
Sustainability Officer, the targets and strategies are submitted 
to the Board. The two routine meetings each year are also used 
to keep committee members up to date on the progress and 
outcomes of each functional team.
To demonstrate our commitment to carbon resolution, Compal 
has already committed to 100% use of renewable energy by 
2050 and becomed the RE100 member. Our SBT configuration 
has been completed and submitted to SBTi as well. At the same 
time, Compal is calling upon our value chain and partners 
to join us in supporting biodiversity and forest conservation 
in response to the environmental and ecological challenges 
brought by climate change. We have issued our Biodiversity and 
No-Deforestation Policy. The Policy is applicable to Compal and 
all global subsidiaries in which we hold more a stake of more 
than 50% and operational control.

4.1.2 Compal Environment Sustainability Policy
Compal seeks the balance and sustainable development 
of the environment, society, and economy. We understand 
that Compal products, services, and business activities may 
impact on the environment. That is why we have made 
“Environmental Sustainability” and “Responsible Manufacturing” 
our starting point to actively reduce our environmental 
impact through “Climate Change Mitigation and Adaptation”, 
“Water Management”, “Energy Management”, and “Waste 
Management” in order to realize our goal of environmental 
sustainability.
We promise:
To comply with environmental protection and other relevant 
laws and regulations, and to also require the compliance of 
our value chain and business partners (including suppliers, 
service providers, contractors, outsourcing companies, and 
logistic providers), as well as the companies being acquired 
(including during the due diligence and merger process).
The Environmental Managerment Unit oversees the 
implementation, guided by the top management. Annual 
targets, quantitative indicators and action plans are 
established to execute various environmental sustainability 
projects. Regular tracking of these targets and outcomes is 
employed to continually improve operational efficiency and 
reduce environmental impacts.
We invest in corporate environmental and sustainability 
education so that employees understand their role and 
recognize their obligations; we foster a healthy green 
lifestyle for employees, boost their environmental 
awareness, and encourage their participation in the 
implementation of environmental policies.

o
o
CHAPTER

Sustainability Report
2023
 075
Development of products that are aligned with global trends 
and the building of customer trust are the keys to sustainable 
corporate development. The Compal product design philosophy 
is based on the “Product Life Cycle.”The potential environmental 
impacts that our products may cause at different stages of their 
life cycle are taken into account, starting from the purchase 
of raw materials, manufacturing, shipping/delivery, usage by 
consumers and ending with disposal and recycling. During the 
product design phase, our R&D team not only pays attention 
user requirements, functionality and added value but also 
strives for “minimization of environmental burden”at every 
stage. Product development and design therefore follows 
this approach. We also assist customers with applying for 
environmental labels that include life cycle assessment based on 
the requirements of their sales region.
In 2023,79 products passed EPEAT including 56 Gold (EPEAT 
2018) medals. 15 products also passed Taiwan’s environmental 
labeling requirements, demonstrating the proactive action taken 
by Compal in product design and manufacturing as well as the 
establishment of a product development and design philosophy 
based around environmental protection.

Sound and open channels of communication are 
established to convey to employees, value chain partners, 
business partners, local residents, and other internal/
external stakeholders the targets and values of the 
Compal environmental sustainability policy.
Policy implementation and management: 
Green products and services: Develop environmentally 
friendly products and promote the circular economy
Green manufacturing and operations: Implementation 
of energy-efficient, water-efficient, and waste reducing 
operating models, gradual replacement of energy- and 
water-intensive equipment, introduction of automated 
production equipment, development of renewable energy, 
and practicing source reduction for waste
Green transportation and logistics: Optimization of 
packaging design for packaging and plastic reduction; 
reduce packaging dimensions to improve transportation 
efficiency and reduce energy consumption during 
transportation
Green partners and cooperation: The selection of 
business partners (including suppliers, service providers, 
contractors, outsourcing companies, logistics operators) 
and companies targeted for merger and acquisition 
(including during the due diligence and merger & 
acquisition period) takes their environment-related 
policies or commitments into consideration. Preference 
is given to those with targets and philosophy similar to 
Compal’s environmental sustainability policy.

Sustainability Report
2023
 076
In terms of green design and patents, Compal draws up 
decades of industry experience and has established a product 
design philosophy that conforms to the circular economy. 
The core strategies include material selection, energy-efficient 
design, and ease of disassembly. These are all important 
elements for the realization of a circular economy. At the same 
time, we pay close attention to international trends as well 
as stakeholder/customer requirements. We aim to optimize 
the ecological performance through eco-friendly design. In 
addition, we launched internal innovation challenges that 
incentivize employees through prize money and awards in 
order to identify more possibilities.
To progressively realize the goals of the circular economy, 
the Company now requires business notebook compute 
products to use more than 5% recycled materials. This target 
aims to encourage the recovery and reuse of products at the 
end of their service life in order to reduce resource waste 
and environmental impact. The Company has successfully 
developed 36 compliant R&D models and put them into mass 
production so far in a demonstration of our commitment to 
environmental responsibility
Full Material Disclosure
The implementation of Full Material Disclosure (FMD) is essential to 
ensure that products pose no threat to the environment or user health 
and safety against the backdrop of global consensus, corporate targets, 
and net zero carbon emission trends. Suppliers are required to disclose 
the types of chemical substances and their concentrations for all 
homogenous substances (Project FMD reached:  99.23%). In the future, a 
comprehensive system can be planned that combines carbon footprint, 
carbon neutrality and related systems to prepare for new requirements in 
national regulations.
Outstanding Energy Efficiency and Use of 
Environmentally Friendly Materials
Aspire Vero retains the low power consumption of its predecessor. 
Energy consumption is also 35% lower than the previous generation of 
products.
The ecological design of Aspire Vero takes the Earth’s environment into 
full account. The product emphasizes sustainable development and 
reduces CO2 emissions by 30%. It is not only easy to recycle but can 
also adapt to Earth’s requirements. To increase public awareness on Post 
Consumer Recycled (PCR) plastics, Aspire Vero increased PCR usage in 
the chassis to 40%. PCR usage in the key caps and PSU casing were also 
increased to 50%. Touch panel used 100% recycled marine materials 
and 100% recyclable/reusable eco-packaging. At the same time, we 
maintained the quality and durability of manufacturing to extend the 
device’s service life. Since the product is made from PCR, Aspire Vero 
is estimated to have kept at least 30 tCO₂e of wast plastics out of the 
landfill (the equivalent to 96,000 5L water containers). Reduction of waste 
plastics is also continuing to grow.

ACER Aspire Vero

 077
Vanguard in Climate Change Mitigation - Conformity 
with EPEAT Climate+
EPEAT Climate+ was recently launched by Global Electronic Council, the 
US non-profit environmental protection organization. The goal is reduce 
the impact of GHG emissions or energy usage by electronic products 
during the design and manufacturing phase. For example, a brand 
vendor may announced reducing carbon emission targets and require 
a certain percentage of renewal energy to be used. The production 
facilities for the supply chain of key components must possess ISO 50001 
energy management system certification. Corporate GHG inventories 
must also be verified by a third-party body.
Latitude 5440 was one of the first models to be registered on the EPEAT 
Climate+ list to provide consumers with more sustainable and eco-
friendly product, and achieve the target for climate change.
Use of Eco-Friendly Materials and Outstanding Energy 
Efficiency
Latitude 9440 2-in-1 is a business computer equipped with a zero-lattice 
keyboard that reduces keyboard power consumption by up to 75%. 
This exceeds the 66% energy efficiency required by the US Energy Star 
Certification. The improvement in energy efficiency also reduces carbon 
emissions so the product is more eco-friendly and has less of an impact 
on the environment. Material selection took materials friendly to the 
planet into account. The entire machine uses Halogen-free materials 
(but not the power cables and PSU), voluntarily eliminated the use of 
Halogen-based flame retardant to reduce damage to the Ozone Layer. 
We use low-carbon, 75% cases for recovering aluminum materials, and 
increased the percentage of Post-Consumer Recycled (PCR) to over 25%. 
In addition to letting consumers will not only enjoy premium technology, 
we also hold the “EPEAT Gold” eco-label assessment and “TCO” voluntary 
certification. We will stay true to our management responsibility on 
green products and reduce the environmental impact of products during 
their product life cycle and realize the sustainable development of the 
environment.
DELL Latitude 5440
DELL Latitude 9440 2-in-1
Image Source: Product Official Website.
Image Source: Product Official Website.
Outstanding Energy Conservation Performance
The B5RPL series NB has obtained third-party Energy Star certification. 
Its outstanding energy efficiency conforms to EPEAT Gold and surpasses 
the 40% standard set by Energy Star. It therefore reduces pollution from 
electricity consumption while providing consumers with an exceptional 
energy-efficiency experience.
Full Material Disclosure
To provide users with a better understanding of the materials used 
throughout the product, suppliers are required to submit a positive list 
of the chemical substances used in all parts and components. Double 
control and supervision was enforced through a combination of the FMD 
system and Compal’s internal product material management system to 
provide disclosure in excess of 90%. The associated databases were also 
enhanced to improve transparency and meet the requirements of future 
laws and environmental standards.
ASUS B5402CV/FV series | B5602CV series

 078
Proactively Eliminate the Use of Halogenated Flame 
Retardants to Reduce Ozone Layer Depletion
Environmentally Friendly Materials, High Proportion of Material Waste 
Reduction and Recycling and Exceptional Energy Efficiency
Eco-friendly materials were selected for this model with halogen-free 
materials (excluding the power cable and power supply unit) used 
throughout. The use of halogen-based flame retardants was proactively 
eliminated to reduce ozone layer depletion. Up to 30% of the plastic 
parts were made from recycled materials including reclaimed marine 
plastics. Electronic products are therefore no longer reclaimed through 
a closed loop. Even when a product is no longer useful, up to 97% 
of the machine’s weight in materials and components can still be 
remanufactured by the recovery system or regenerated to become other 
materials in order to fulfill the waste reduction and circular economy 
process.In terms of product energy efficiency and endurance, the product 
is 49% more energy efficient than the standard set by the US Energy Star. 
Energy efficiency has therefore been improved with active efforts made 
to reduce carbon emissions as well, resulting in a more environmentally 
product and less impact on the environment.
The casing is made from 100% recycled aluminum materials. Recycling 
of materials and software services was improved to extend the 
product life cycle and reduce our impact on the environment. Waste 
and plastic reduction was introduced. For the previous products, we 
reduced the packaging and removed the waste plastics. Over 99% of 
packaging materials are made from non-plastic materials to reduce 
their environmental impact.
Automated testing tools were introduced during the development 
phase of the 5G product development stage and replace expensive 
equipment expenses with software programming. The optimization of 
the labor-intensive testing process requires a large number of workers 
and confirmation of 100% consistency. 5G RAN testing was carried 
out in the Multi UE testing and acceptance tool. This very significant 
optimization of the test workflow will not only conserve internal costs. 
Programs can also be installed on the NB to reduce production and 
power consumption by hardware, and help with reducing carbon 
emissions.
HP ENVY 17.3 inch Laptop PC
Google Pixel 7a
5GREAT System (5G RAN E2E Auto Test System)

04.2.2 Green Patents
 079
As a manufacturing company dedicated to innovative research 
and development, Compal encourages employees to engage 
in research, invention, and innovation related to products. 
This enhances the achievements in technology research and 
development, improves the quality and functionality of the 
company’s products, strengthens its competitiveness, and 
explores opportunities for future development.
Duties and Responsibilities
The patent department is primarily responsible for ensuring 
legal protection for creative ideas from R&D team during the 
process of product development through means of patent 
application. Employees can submit their patent applications 
through the Company’s online system. Submissions are to 
be reviewed by the Patent Advisory Committee in order to 
determine if application should be made for the proposal. For 
proposals that enter the Advisory Committee, the inventor and 
the co-inventor receive a proposal bonus for encouragement. 
By discussing relevant processes with R&D personnel, patent 
personnel can help by suggesting or assisting with the 
direction of R&D and better understand the current status 
of technological development for competitors or potential 
customers. In addition, Compal also provides relevant bonuses 
and incentives for patents (proposal/application incentive, 
patent registration bonus, reuse bonus and so forth) as a way 
to encourage R&D employees to proactively devote themselves 
to re-innovation and thereby facilitate positive development in 
their careers.
Education Training
In order to help employees gain more in-depth knowledge on 
patent development, Compal has designed and implemented 
its “Orientation for R&D Personnel - Overview on Patents” 
to introduce new R&D employees to concepts on trademark 
rights, copyrights and patent rights along with fundamental 
knowledge on confidentiality when participating in projects 
to help new employees familiarize themselves with patents. 
Should R&D Department deem it necessary, Patent Department 
will design advanced training courses tailored to the need. By 
illustrating and sharing different patent themes for different 
functional departments, the employees will be able to deepen 
their knowledge on patents.

 081
Notebook projects and ESG-related patents accounted for 12% of all patents. The example of eco-
friendly patents are provided for reference.
Patent Name/Publication No./Patent No.
Design Description for Environmentally-friendly Patents
Simulated testing system and simulated test model I824624
This invention offers a simulation testing system and simulated testing method. Simulation testing system 
includes the control devices, power configuration devices, and data capture device. The control device 
generations scenario control signals based on the multitude of scenarios on offer. The power supply 
configuration device responds to the scenario control signal by generating either a simulated charging 
source or simulated load. The simulated charging power supply and/or simulated load must be provided to 
the device under test. The test device is then set to react to the simulated charging source and/or simulated 
load in order to generate test data. Data capture device captures test data and provides it to the control 
device. The testing system in this invention can improve testing efficiency and realize the goals of energy 
conservation and reducing carbon emission.
Portable Electronic Device and its Method of Sterilization and Disinfection I807267
A portable electronic devices that includes one primary unit, one secondary unit, one cam structure, one 
control unit, one sensor unit, one sterilization unit, and one shielding module. Primary unit contains one 
primary inside surface. Secondary unit contains one secondary inside surface. Cam structure is connected 
between the primary unit and secondary unit. The control unit is configured within the primary unit or 
secondary unit. The sensor unit is configured within the primary unit or secondary unit, and coupled to the 
control unit. The sterilization module is configured in the cam structure and coupled to the couple unit. It 
generates light for sterilization and disinfection. The shielding module is configured on the cam structure and 
can move relative to the cam structure. The disinfection/sterilization structure and method designed for the 
electronic device in this invention removes the need for use of large sterilization/disinfection machines. The 
goal of energy efficiency and reducing carbon emission can then be achieved.
Modular Chiller Device I815506
A type of modular chiller device that is used for cooling the heatsink model inside an electronic device. 
Modular chiller device must include one constant temperature module and at least one external module. The 
constant temperature module contains a casing and a constant temperature device. One end of the constant 
temperature chip is configured within the casing. The other end protrudes outside of the casing. At least one 
external module is assigned to the constant temperature module. The other end of the constant temperature 
chip should be in contact with the base of the cooling module. At least one external module has a casing that 
is suitable for the stacking of constant temperature modules. The mechanical design of this event improves 
the cooling efficiency of thin electronic devices in order to extend the service life of internal electronic 
devices.
Electronic Device I804317
An electronic device that consists of one primary unit, one secondary unit, one pivot module, one cover unit, 
and one support panel. The primary unit includes an internal space and one vent. The vent is connected to the 
internal space. The secondary unit can be rotated to connect to the primary unit. The pivot module contains 
one primary end and one secondary end. The primary end is coupled to the primary unit and the secondary 
end is connected to the secondary unit. The cover unit can slide and is configured on the secondary unit. The 
support panel can be rotated to connect to the cover unit and also slid to connect to the pivot module. When 
the primary unit and secondary unit are both expanded, the support panel moves along the pivot module and 
protrudes beyond the primary unit. The support unit also makes the cover unit move along the secondary 
unit to form a heat exhaust port. The mechanical design of this event improves the cooling efficiency of thin 
electronic devices in order to extend the service life of internal electronic devices.
Power Supply Management Device and Management Method I815233
The proposal of a power supply management device and management method. The power supply 
management devices consists of a power switch, detection circuit, and controller. The power supply switch is 
connected to an external power supply. The detection circuit is connected to the internal power supply and at 
least one operating power supply. The detection circuit determines whether the internal power supply and/
or operating supply is within the pre-defined specifications for generating the protected activation signal. 
The controller sets protection flags based on the protected activation signal and executes the corresponding 
application program to generate control signals based on the protection flag. The controller is used to 
transmit the control signal and cut off the power switch. The device and management method proposed in 
this invention will protect electronic devices from damage due to anomalies in the power supply, and thus 
ensure the operational safety of electronic devices.
Integrated Battery Module I798126
A type of integrated module - air patch battery that can be attached to one device body that includes a 
controller/charging module, a wrappable battery connected to the controller/charging module, as well as 
connector and casing attached to the device body. The casing includes a primary section for holding the air 
patch battery, and a secondary section for holding the controller/charging module. Additionally, at least part 
of the length of the primary section can be bent to the primary curvature radius. At least of the length of the 
secondary section can also be bent and the secondary curvature radius. When an electronic devices uses the 
integrated battery module proposed in this invention, the operating temperature of the electronic device is 
reduced, extending the service life of components within the electronic device.
Thermal Module and Electronic Device I815016
A thermal module suitable for the electronic device. The thermal module consists of a heatsink structure 
and cooling fan. The heatsink structure is integrated into the casing of the electronic device and contains a 
heatsink component. A thermal channel is formed between the heatsink component and outer casing. The 
cooling fan is located next to the heatsink component. The cooling fan or heatsink structure includes an air 
flow guide which has open channels connected to the thermal channels. The cooling fan provides cooling air 
flow, and the air flow guide directs the cooling air flow asymmetrically along the exhaust side of the cooling 
fan where it passes through the open channels connected to the cooling channels. The mechanical design 
of this event improves the cooling efficiency of thin electronic devices in order to extend the service life of 
internal electronic devices.

 082
Compal has continued to host the “Innovation Competition” since 2017 with large cash prizes and 
public award ceremonies as incentives. Employees are encourage to participate in the contest to 
promote improvements and innovations in management, work flows and product R&D. Employees 
can make suggestions and proposals important to the development of the Company through the 
competition. The proposals are implemented after judging to improve management efficiency, 
optimize processes, and promote innovation.
The competition not only recognizes employees for their efforts but also serves as an important 
platform for exchange of ideas and promotion of the Company’s development. The Company 
is continuing to take on employee suggestions as well as optimize our systems and processes 
to make innovation a part of our corporate DNA, improve organizational productivity and 
competitiveness, and realize a win-win outcome.
The “ESG x Innovation Bonus”was introduced in 2022 to inspire employee interest in corporate ESG 
goals, encourage sustainable design, and promote cross-department collaboration. Employees can 
propose practical concepts for helping the Company realize the goal of net zero emissions.
To this end, an ESG preliminary judging panel was formed responsible for defining the ESG scoring 
mechanism and conducting the preliminary assessment. At the same time, the preliminary judging 
team also conducts in-depth analysis of innovative proposals that show ESG potential and offer 
advice on proposal writing. Instructors with expert knowledge of ESG are also invited to host 
seminars. The seminars are aimed at enhancing employee understanding and practice of ESG. They 
help proposal authors examine their own innovation proposals as well as its relevance to ESG.
At the same time, the program also emphasized the importance of dialog. Employees are 
encouraged to cultivate sound communication skills and expected to respond effectively to the 
needs and concerns of internal/external stakeholders. Compal hopes to popularize ESG ideals 
throughout the entire organization through these measures and promote the development of the 
Company in a more sustainable direction.
Innovation Competition
The 2023 award presentation ceremony was incorporated in to the Company’s annual end-of-
year party. This not only served to emphasize the importance of the Innovation Competition but 
also our approval and recognition of employee contributions to the Company.

04.3 Raw Material Management
04.3.1 Full Material Declaration
 083
In an effort to deliver quality products that promote health 
and safety without compromising issues on human rights and 
environmental protection, Compal has taken steps to ensure 
that all products are compliant to pertinent international 
regulations, directives and customer demands right from the 
stage of design and development through systematic control 
that is made possible with our Integrated System for Product 
Development (ISPD). Not only that, we have also continued to 
use the COMPAL Supplier Design Collaboration Portal System 
for the purposes of material composition investigation. In 
light of updates to our customers’ environmental protection 
standards, the latest requirements in global environmental 
laws and upgrade to Compal’s green product management 
system, some of our plants even adopted QC 080000 hazardous 
substance process management.
Compal’s aim for customers’ health and safety was not only to 
comply with the customer’s demands and protect customer’s 
safety; the development of Halogen-free products and 
construction of a more robust production capacity are our 
promise and responsibility. All product materials have now 
achieved compliance with the relevant chemical requirements 
and human rights topics. Each management approach is 
outlined below: 
04.3.1 Full Material Declaration
International attention to chemical management means that 
chemical regulations are now being updated with increasing 
frequency and cover more items as well. Compal responded to 
this trend by evaluating the feasibility of full material declaration 
(FMD) and data collection in 2015.
Under the traditional material management method, a 
controlled material list is published by Compal listing all 
restricted substances. Vendors then check each item on the 
list to see if they comply with the Compal controlled material 
standard. This type of negative listing allow vendors to check 
whether the parts they supply comply with current regulations. 
Since only a declaration is made on controlled substances, if 
materials not in the Compal standard is added to international 
regulations then there is a gap in control until Compal standards 
are updated.
FMD asks the vendor to disclose all materials in their part 
rather than just the items specified in the Compal controlled 
material standard. All chemical materials and their proportions 
within the product must be listed. Once there is FMD for all 
parts in a product, a full picture of the product’s chemical 
composition emerges so that changes in material regulations 
and requirements can be responded to in a timely manner.
There were three projects in the first lot to implement FMD after 
the system went live. At the time, disclosure rate was 25% of 
the product weight. Continued communication with suppliers, 
internal education & training, and system improvements saw 65 
projects achieve 90% disclosure by Notebook product weight 
in 2023. The number of projects and disclosure rate have held 
steady. In the future, Compal will continued to collect FMDs 
for more parts and components then compile them into a 
complete and transparent materials database. We will engage 
in the proactive identification and analysis of high-risk materials 
to ensure that the products we manufacture are friendly to the 
environment and human health.

Hazardous Substance Management
A series of effective measures were adopted by Compal to 
reduce product impact on customer health and the environment. 
Controls were implemented by Compal from material selection 
onwards with the relevant chemical requirements incorporated 
into the management regulations. These included but are 
not limited to the EU Registration, Evaluation, Authorisation 
and Restriction of Chemicals (REACH) directive, and the EU 
Restriction of Hazardous Substances Directive (RoHS) directive. 
Material declarations are also periodically updated in accordance 
with the IEC 624742 international materials declaration standard.
To manage hazardous substances more effectively, reduce the 
risk of fraudulent reports, as well as improve management 
quality and efficiency, we now upload digital hazardous 
substance reports to the database of third-party certification 
bodies. Digital reports accounted for 44% in 2023. Continued 
efforts should see this ratio increased to 60% in 2024.
To familiarize suppliers and R&D personnel with the latest 
standards, e-mail announcements and online courses were 
adopted in 2023 to ensure that design and parts conformed 
with the relevant management standards. Such measures help to 
ensure product safety and environmental friendliness while also 
improving the transparency and traceability of the supply chain.
CHAPTER

Sustainability Report
2023
 084
EU REACH
REACH (Registration, Evaluation, and Authorization of 
Chemicals) is a set of regulations imposed by the European 
Union to control imported chemical substances. REACH 
controls use and importation of chemical substances by 
implementing a series of measures including registration, 
evaluation, authorization, and mandatory disclosure. Compal 
requires suppliers to make full disclosure of SVHC contents in 
all supplied parts, and encourages them to take step towards 
reducing and eliminating uses of such substances as early as 
possible. Compal also includes the hazardous chemicals listed 
in Annex XIV of the EU chemicals policy into its environmental 
management regulations, restricting their usage. Compal 
periodically revises its environmental management regulations 
in accordance with updated international requirements 
regarding hazardous substances.
Restriction of Hazardous Substances (RoHS) directive
In light of increasing harm to the environment caused by waste 
electronics and appliances, the European Union implemented 
RoHS (Restriction of the use of Certain Hazardous Substances 
Directive) in 2002 that imposed controls over the concentration 
of 6 hazardous substances: lead (Pb), mercury (Hg), Cadmium 
(Cd), hexavalent chromium (Cr6+), polybrominated biphenyls 
(PBB) and polybrominated diphenyl ethers (PBDE). Compal 
products are 100% complaint with all limits set by the RoHS 
directive. There were no returns due to RoHS violations.
Halogen-Free 
As halogen compounds release substances toxic to the 
environment and organisms after incomplete combustion, 
EU has included chlorinated and brominated flame retardant 
as a controlled substance in the RoHS directive. In light of 
the voluntary standards - “halogen-free parts and processes” 
introduced by international organizations and customers’ 
increasingly stringent demands on environmental protection, 
Compal has amended the management standards for 
environmental-related substances controlled in parts and 
materials to regulate halogen (chlorine/bromine) content, and 
is constantly improving its production systems to eliminate 
halogen altogether for the benefit of the environment and 
human health.
Compal began introducing Halogen-free parts and production 
processes in 2007. All major brand customers are now 
transitioning to Halogen-free eco-friendly specifications. 
Some of the production technologies have now matured 
and alternative materials that do not impact on product 
performance are now available. Compal will continue to 
upgrade our part management and design abilities, and 
accelerate the obsolescence of parts that contain Halogen in 
accordance with market trends.
Research, development, and mass production of Halogen-free 
wearable devices was launched in 2017. We have continued to 
develop more eco-friendly products, with a total of 73 Halogen-
free products developed and put into mass production in 2023.

04.4 Green Manufacturing
 085
With growing global awareness for environmental protection, 
green production has become the most crucial component in 
the maintenance of environmental resources and corporate 
competitiveness. And as such, Compal continues to adhere to its 
tried-and-true approach to green production while improving 
on its existing operating models of energy-conservation, water-
conservation and waste-reduction.
Legal Compliance
Compliance is fundamental to corporate responsibility. Proper 
compliance is essential to the steady growth and sustainability 
of an enterprise. Environmental protection is prioritized at 
Compal. Our plants are spread across Taiwan, China, Vietnam, 
and Brazil. Any environmental disputes will have an immediate 
impact on our operations and business reputation.
Compal has a defined Environmental Safety policy. There are 
personnel at each plant assigned to collate environmental, 
safety, and health regulations on a monthly basis and forward 
them to the relevant personnel. Personnel are then tasked to 
review and amend any affected operations and regulations to 
bring them up to date. Amendments may also be proposed 
at any time if there are any major legislative changes that 
require the amendment of related company policies, goals, and 
standards.
To effectively manage the operational challenges related 
to the environment that Compal may face, we start with 
quantification and gradually build, manage, and implement 
an environmental management system. All of our plants have 
obtained third-party ISO 14001 certification, and are obtaining 
ISO 14064-1 and ISO 50001 certifications in separate stages. 
Through third-party inspection and audits, we ensure that the 
company has effectively established systems and processes to 
track and manage various environmental performance metrics. 
This enhances energy use efficiency, actively implements 
waste reduction, and promotes zero waste to landfill. Various 
grievance channels are also provided to supply products and 
services that meet stakeholder expectations in a consistent and 
stable manner. Environmental compliance as well as continued 
improvement and effective management are expected of all 
Compal production processes and products. There were no 
violations of environmental laws in 2023.

04.4.1 Energy-Saving Production
 086
We have invested in R&D personnel and funds to develop the “Energy and Environmental Monitoring” platform, and continue to 
optimize its functions. By monitoring energy consumption in real-time, the platform tracks daily energy usage budgets based on 
production capacity, enabling timely energy management and the implementation of energy-saving measures, thereby effectively 
reducing energy consumption. We innovate new methods to improve energy efficiency, selecting energy-saving products when 
replacing high-energy-consuming equipment, and actively introducing external advisory units. The Pingzhen, Kunshan Plants 3, 
Chengdu Plant, and Chongqing CQ and CQA plants have all obtained ISO 50001 Energy managerment system certification. We also 
promote equipment networking with the expectation of maximizing the economic benefits of each unit’s energy use, aligning with 
the goals of the EP100 initiative.
Note: EP100 is an initiative led by The Climate Group, CDP, and the Global Alliance for Energy Productivity. It is a collaborative effort 
encouraging global companies to pledge to maximize the economic benefits derived from each unit of energy used.

CHAPTER

Energy Management
Energy-Conservation and Environmental Protection 
Measures at Our Plants
Sustainability Report
2023
 087
Each plant uses an energy KPI to keep track of energy usage, 
and results are reviewed and improved upon on a monthly 
basis. Total energy consumption in 2023 was 1,204,076 GJ and 
energy intensity was 1.27. Non-renewable energy consumption 
amounted to 633,821.8 GJ, and renewable energy consumption 
amounted to 570, 254.4 GJ.     
Compal promotes energy-saving projects across its various 
plants. It has implemented ISO 50001 management system 
certification in 5 plants, inviting energy professional assessment 
firms to measure and identify inefficiencies, thereby enhancing 
energy efficiency. Starting from 2023,Compal initiated the 
deployment of an intelligent algorithm-based air conditioning 
system at its Pingzhen plant. This system integrates advanced 
smart algorithms to optimize operational strategies applied to air 
conditioning systems. By leveraging technologies such as data 
mining, performance alerts, and weather forecasting integrated 
into the digital air conditioning management system, Compal 
actively manages building energy consumption. This proactive 
approach aims to achieve optimized operation modes for air 
conditioning systems, targeting energy savings of 5-12%. Compal 
plans to extend these results and experiences to all its plants.
Comparison of Electricity Energy Usage Intensity 
The energy usage intensity (EUI) of 350 kWh per Million NTD in 
revenue was 3 kWh lower than 2022. Despite the reduction in 
power consumption from aggressive energy-saving initiatives, 
continued adjustments to production plants as part of our 
business strategy meant EUI reduction targets were not met. 
Compal will therefore engage in even more aggressive energy 
resource management and tracking, boost the use of renewable 
energy, and reduce our demand for non-renewable energy. More 
details will be provided in the chapter on climate change.
Compal is not in an energy-intensive industry but active 
efforts are still being made to improve energy usage on 
the production line. Production line automation and the 
installation of connective systems make the current status of 
equipment from different stages available online to facilitate 
remote monitoring and management.
The maintenance of air-conditioning (AC) and lighting 
at reasonable levels is the pre-requisite to energy saving 
initiatives. Phased upgrade to energy-saving lighting, fitting 
sensors to less-frequented areas, and standalone switches 
in each partitioned area were adopted. Laboratories were 
equipped with stand-alone AC equipment as part of the 
plant’s continued efforts on energy conservation. The energy 
conservation education strategy is tabled below for reference.
Environmental Protection Measures at the Plant

o	 Set standard for energy unit per unit of production. Daily

o	 The energy monitoring and control platform was introduced 
at the Pingzhen Plant in 2023. An energy inventory 
metered usage determined that energy efficiency of the 
air conditioning water system can be improved by 5-12% 
through a series of improvements including the introduction 
of digital AC management to optimize operating modes, 
integration of data mining, performance early warning, 
and weather forecasting techniques into the digital AC 
management system, and active energy management in 
buildings to optimize AC system operations.
Compal is implementing smart algorithms in its air conditioning 
systems and integrating smart meters with IoT communication 
technology. Digital metering devices capture data through IoT 
communication technology, allowing the system’s backend 
analysis module to calculate energy flow, usage statistics, and 
comparative reports on discrepancies. These are provided 
to end-users and consulting teams for discussion on future 
electricity management strategies. Factory Affairs personnel 
can use the operating strategy recommended by the system 
to optimize the parameters so that the energy supply is better 
aligned with the plant’s requirements and realize intelligent 
energy utilization.
