Resources and guides for new employees
We hope that new employees can adapt to 
their new role and master the required skills 
and concepts as quickly as possible so they 
immediately undergo a series of new employees 
training courses once they join the Company. The 
mentor system also provides one-to-one training 
to help new employees adapt to the Compal 
culture and shorten the learning curve. New 
employees are offered a new employees support 
survey one month after they start work to ensure 
timely assistance if necessary. We also reach 
out to all new employees in R&D units through 
e-newsletters. In addition to providing new 
employees with useful resources and guides, we 
also continue to emphasize their importance and 
welcome them to the Company one, two and three 
months after their arrival through the e-newsletter.

Potential Talent Assessment and Individual 
Development Plan (IDP)
Sustainability Report
2023
 133
The Compal Individual Development Plan (IDP) 
is a personalized development plan based on 
the Compal Core Model supplemented by 
professional assessment tools. An objective and 
systematic mechanism is used to identify key 
talents (including potential talent, junior/middle 
management).
To cultivate and establish a pool of quality 
talent in a more comprehensive manner, two-
way communication and discussions with key 
talent and their direct supervisors are conducted 
to co-develop key development targets for 
the year. Different development methods are 
utilized (including: training courses, regular 
one-to-one interviews, long-term coaching, 
or task assignments) and auxiliary systems 
used to conduct two follow-up and reviews of 
development outcomes and plan progress each 
year (mid-year and end-of-year). A positive 
feedback mechanism is encouraged and enforced 
so that potential talent and managers under 
development can hone their own strengths or 
target areas, demonstrate the key behaviors 
sought by the Company, and ultimately produce 
changes in behavior. In response to talent 
requirements of long-term organizational 
development, supervisors may also increase the 
IDP planning and review frequency for general 
employees by agile conversations, and adjust 
the development plan as necessary. Sustained 
development planning and skills cultivation will 
contribute to the overall talent pool at Compal.
A total of 2,207 employees took part in 
this program in 2023. The retention rate of 
participating employees reached 98.4% as well. 
The program is therefore conducive to the 
continued forging of quality talent, building 
of key knowledge, and improving of overall 
competitiveness at Compal.

Shen-Geng Training Program
Internal (external) speakers from different 
functions were invited to host seminars on 
pioneering, trends, market and academic 
information in the spirit of experience 
sharing. In addition to the implementation 
of competency development for employees 
in R&D-related units, promotion of lifelong 
learning and growth, and inspiring the 
passing on and exchange of R&D experience, 
we also encouraged employees to engage in 
trans-function learning so their knowledge 
and experience can be reused and preserved. 
A total of 44 classes were held during 2023 
with a total attendance of 4,483 people. 52 
internal (external) instructors were invited 
to share their professional knowledge. Up 
to 64.09% of employees were engaged in 
trans-function learning. At the same time, a 
competition to select and publicly recognize 
good instructors is held in December every 
year to encourage employees to become 
instructors.

Cultivation of Specialists at Kunshan Plant
Local government in Kunshan, China, 
encourages businesses to participate in pre-
serve training, and technicians to take part in 
specialist training. The program is open to all 
employees with less than one year’s service. In 
2023, 261 took part in government-directed 
pre-service training courses and subsidies. Also 
in 2023, 639 employees undertook specialist 
training and received technical certification in 
industrial robotics, industrial vision, drafting, 
computer repairs, and computer programming. 
These included 18 employees that were 
recognized for “Outstanding Contribution”by 
the Kunshan Municipal Government and eligible 
for government stipend. Percentage of total 
employees that undertook certification training: 
6.3%. Course satisfaction was 97%.

6.2.4 Diverse Performance Appraisal Modes
 135
Performance 
Appraisal Items
Subject
Frequency
Description
Periodic Performance Appraisal
Periodic performance appraisal are conducted 
to enforce Compal, departmental and individual 
goals. These include annual performance 
appraisals, employee probation period 
appraisals, project appraisals, and so on. 
Employee performance is measured through 
the definition of fair and impartial metrics. 
Through the performance reviews, Compal 
can ensure that employee performance meets 
the company’s expectations and standards. 
Problems can also be identified and improved 
upon in a timely manner. At the same time, 
reviews promote two-way communication 
between the company and the employees 
so managers can provide subordinates with 
guidance and assistance more quickly. Overall 
productivity is improved and the long-term 
development goals of Compal can be realized.
New Employees
All Employees
Managers in Taiwan 
(including expatriates)

Units and Their 
Employees

well as Managers or

Development
Intern
R&D Project Team
Probation reviews are used to establish the suitability of new employees for their current 
position. Suitable personnel are offered “regular employment”while unsuitable personnel 
receive either “extension of probation” or “termination of probation” in accordance with the 
probation system.
Performance appraisal are designed to enforce Company/departmental/individual targets/
strategies/approach and establish a performance-oriented appraisal system. The system 
assists teams with realizing their performance targets, promotes proper employment 
and application of talent within the organization, and enhances the overall quality and 
professionalism of employees in order to create business growth for the Company.
The appraisal is aimed at strengthening teamwork between departments and breaking 
down inter-departmental barriers/parochialism. Department and division heads assess and 
provide feedback on each other from a multi-disciplinary and diversity perspective each year. 
Obtaining more objective and substantive metrics help supervisors overcome management 
blind spots. The metrics can also be used by the annual performance appraisal.
KPIs are defined for designated business units and linked to the performance system every 
year to promote organizational development, realize organizational targets, and implement 
technological development. These encompass business-related indicators (e.g. profits, 
profitability) and organizational development indicators (e.g. innovation). Business units with 
a higher completion rate receive a higher quota of better performance appraisals. Supervisors 
also evaluate performance distribution of teams when evaluating the performance of 
individual team members.
Development targets are jointly set by the development candidate and their supervisor at the 
start of the year. Development outcomes and progress undergo two reviews (mid-year and 
end-of-year) each year. A positive feedback mechanism and agile conversations is encouraged 
and enforced so that candidates can hone their own strengths or target areas. The process 
and outcomes of the IDP can also be used as key references during their performance 
appraisal to realize the strategy of combining talent cultivation with performance.
The supervisor and intern jointly sets targets based on the type of internship. One to three 
performance reviews are then conducted.
A series of appraisal are conducted by the organizational supervisor for that project based 
on the project’s strategic objectives and the actual performance, as well as the overall 
professionalism and competency demonstrated by project team members during the project.

Compal’s Research and Development Center in Taipei first 
introduced Six Sigma in 2002. It has accumulated more than 
twenty years of experience with the application of Six Sigma’s 
logic and tools to education training and projects. The Six 
Sigma logic is used to constantly improve existing procedures; 
LSS (Lean Six Sigma) logic, in particular, contributed to the 
efficiency of our processes, whereas DFSS (Design for Six 
Sigma) logic facilitated newer and better designs.
Six Sigma not only offers real benefits to projects, but also 
helps us to train many talents with a series of e-learning 
courses, on-site courses, and project training. Six Sigma 
workshops were attended 729 times and clocked up 41 
training hours in 2023. Total duration of e-learning was 168.07 
hours with 3,063 people taking part in the online training.

Human Rights Management 
Sustainability Report
2023
06.3 Human Rights Management and Protection
 138
Compal promises to create a working 
environment that respects human rights and 
dignity and incorporates it as one of its core 
values. We insists on complying with the labor-
related laws and regulations of the place where 
it operates, and follows the articles including 
the International Bill of Human Rights, the 
United Nations Guiding Principles on Business 
and Human Rights, the International Labor 
Organization (ILO) Declaration on Fundamental 
Principles and Rights at Work, the OECD 
Guidelines for Multinational Enterprises and the 
United Nations Global Compact. Ten Principles 
(UNGC). Our actions are also consistent with 
the Responsible Business Alliance (RBA) Code 
of Conduct, treating all persons with dignity 
and respect.
To this end, the Human Rights Policy was 
formulated and passed by the Compal Board of 
Directors. Associated management procedures 
were also established. When employees 
sign their employment contract, they are 
immediately covered and protected by a 
collective bargaining agreement. The Company 
plans its attendance system according to 
local laws and employees are given the 
flexibility to take leaves of absence as needed 
without worries. Compal requires all plants 
to harmonize their labor policy with the RBA 
Code of Conduct including the formulation of 
related procedural documents required by the 
Code. Compal also pays constant attention to 
employees’ physical and mental state, work 
performance and family life, and strives to 
create a healthy, safe, comfortable and fully 
equipped work environment.
For child labor and underaged workers, none 
of our plants violated pertinent regulations 
on child labor in 2023. In addition, we have 
also asked all collaborating suppliers to sign 
the “Commitment of Compliance to RBA’s 
Code of Conduct” which explicitly forbids the 
employment of child labor or forced labor and 
the protection of underaged workers’ rights. 
Any suppliers found to have violated RBA’s 
Code of Conduct will be reported to senior 
management for disciplinary actions. 
With regards to the freedom of association, 
pursuant to the Ministry of Labor “Regulations 
for Implementing Labor-Management Meeting” 
and our company “Procedure Governing 
Employees’ Freedom of Association and Right 
to Collective Bargaining“, our employees are 
entitled to freedom of association, participation 
in collective bargaining and peaceful 
negotiations and the right to not take part in 
such activities. There are no unions in Taiwan 
but “Labor-Management Meetings” are held 
in accordance with government regulations. 
Unions have been established in China, 
Vietnam, and Brazil. Union members accounted 
for 63.33% of the total workforce.
Human Rights Policy
o	 Prohibition of any form of forced labor or human trafficking. With advance 
notice according to the law, employees may resign or terminate the employment 
relationship freely.
o	 Prohibition of child labor.
o	 Respect of employees’ freedom of association and right of collective bargaining, and 
provision of channels to express opinions freely.
o	 Compliance with applicable laws and regulations related to salary and working hours, 
provision of fair and reasonable remuneration and working conditions.
o	 Elimination of all forms of discrimination and inhumane treatment, to ensure that all 
personnel have equal job opportunities.
o	 Provision of a safe and healthy working environment, and assistance in maintaining 
physical and mental health for employees.
o	 Commitment to responsible purchasing of minerals.
o	 Compliance with local regulations and accepted international standards.
o	 Provision of independent and anonymous complaint filing mechanism, allowing 
internal and external stakeholders to provide timely feedback and opinion.
o	 Implementation of periodic review and assessment of human rights risk, adoption of 
effective remedial and mitigation actions, andperiodic communication of outcomes 
with external bodies.

6.3.1 Human Rights Due Diligence
 139
Compal has established a human rights due 
diligence process to enforce our human rights 
policy at all operating locations. Human rights 
impact assessments are conducted to identify 
the level of human rights risk at each plant, then 
review and follow-up on improvements. Human 
rights due diligence enhance the integrity 
of all human rights protections and must be 
conducted at least once every three years. The 
human rights due diligence report has already 
been completed. The human rights due diligence 
report including all information on investigation 
policy, process, and activities are published on 
the corporate website in Chinese and English. 
The current investigation is for 2023. The human 
rights due diligence process was formulated in 
2023 and the first Human Rights Due Diligence 
Report was published at the start of 2024. The 
report is now published on the Compal ESG 
website and a follow-up on the risks of material 
topics will be provided at the end of 2024.
Human Rights Due Diligence Process
Establishment (revision) of human rights 
policy
Human rights topic risk assessment and 
identification
Establishment of risk mitigation plans and 
deployment of remedial measures
Periodic review and follow-up 
improvements
Public disclosure of information

Sexual harassment of any form in the workplace 
is strictly prohibited by Compal. Related 
company regulations include Regulations for 
Non-Discrimination and Anti-Harassment Policy, 
Sexual Harassment Prevention Measures, and 
Grievance and Penalties Procedure. There is also 
a complaints mailbox for unlawful infringements 
in the workplace. Any incidents of sexual 
harassment will be dealt with severely; Taiwan 
Headquarters also made training on “prevention 
of sexual harassment” a compulsory part of in-
service seminars for new hires.

 141
Human Rights 
Risk Field
Mitigation Plans
Remediation Actions
1.	Communicate and negotiate with customers effectively, provide appropriate deliv-
ery period in advance.
2.	Implement employee pre-job skills training periodically, in order to increase the-
production efficiency and work skills of employees, and reduce the occurrence of 
overtime.
3.	Gather production line staff to inform them that working hours shall not exceed 60 
hours, and arrange for department assistants to perform internal audits.
4.	Utilize the working hour control system, and send daily messages to inform each 
department about overtime status.
1.	 Set up the workplace in reasonable manner and centralize operations presenting 
occupational hazardous as much as possible, in order to facilitate the monitoring 
and reduction of the scope of hazard.
2.	Implement physical examination and monitoring for employees in job positions 
subject to occupational hazard before, during and leaving their job positions.
3.	For occupational-injury incidents that occur at work, classify the risk level for work-
place job positions of the Company according to the “Four Essential Principles”, in 
order to implement controls according to the risk level. For equipment and facilities 
with existing risk, install effective measures in order to reduce the probability of 
occupational injury.
1.	 Perform relevant operations according to the “Rules Governing Hazardous Opera-
tions”.
2.	Provide qualified protective equipment to operators performing hazardous opera-
tions, and ensure that operators wear such protective equipment properly and have 
the relevant occupational training qualification certificates, prior to perform any 
operation.
3.	Before conducting overhead operations in the plant, it is necessary to obtain EHS 
approval and the approval of the Factory Director of the site.
4.	Depending upon the actual conditions, use other materials or other manufacturing 
processes as alternatives wherever possible. If alternative materials or processes are 
not available, engineering control will be adopted as the primary method of risk 
mitigation, along with personal protective equipment and administrative measures 
as secondary methods, in order to reduce risk of injury.
5.	The plant and its suppliers regularly inspect the operational status of machinery 
and equipment.
6.	Centralized storage of hazardous solutions in a controlled area, with designated 
personnel for management.
1.	 Set up pool of reserve employees or recruit casual workers based on business 
conditions.
2.	According to current orders and manpower, perform production schedule 
optimization and arrange for the shortest feasible period of time for work 
attendance, within the maximum acceptable limit, in order to achieve regulatory 
overtime compliance.
3.	When the working hour control system exceeds 60 logged working hours, the 
system will not accept further completion of the overtime sheet.
1. 	Enhance safety education and training with regard to human-error related 
occupational injury incidents, in order to prevent such errors upon discovery. 
For occupational injuries related to equipment, infrared sensors are installed to 
reduce the occurrence of incidents.
2.	Perform department review, feedback and summarization training for occu-
pational injury incidents that occur, in order to prevent occurrence of similar 
situations.
3.	Utilize relevant results from periodic health examinations of employees to 
discover issues early, implement treatment early, and improve the situation as 
regards workplace health hazards.
4.	Provision of necessary assistance by the Company when an employee suffers an 
occupational injury, traffic accident, or serious illness.
1.	 Implement occupational safety drills and “Forklift Truck Safety Training” and 
“Machinery Safety Training” for employees periodically, and convene supervisor 
safety production meetings in order to share and discuss typical safety incident 
case examples.
2.	Enhance the promotion and regulation of field employees’ wearing of protective 
equipment, and implement field staff inspection of employees’ wearing of 
protective equipment.
3.	Perform detailed inspection before, during and after operations, according to 
the Safety and Health Rules. 
4.	Reduce hazardous operations for employees and outsource such operations to 
external contractors.
5.	Plant site is staffed with designated nurses and first aid personnel in order to 
provide timely emergency and first-aid measures in case of emergencies.

6.3.3 Effective Communication Channels
 142
Compal values the input and opinions of all stakeholders and we have provided relevant griev-
ance channels and mechanisms for stakeholders to implement relevant verification and handling 
of all grievances and complaints in the hopes of listening to different opinions.
Internal Communication Channels
Compal respects the freedom and right of expression for employees. Diverse and open channels 
of communication are employed to build a proactive and constructive labor-management 
relationship. We actively listen and take action in response to employee suggestions. Compal 
establishes its policies not only in compliance with law, but addresses employees’ interests as 
well. Compal has implemented the following communication channels globally to enable two-
way communication and better relations between employees and the employer as below table.
Cases are sent to subordinate units for processing within 24 hours of being received then 
assigned to the dedicated unit for action. We also formulated “Procedure Governing the 
Protection of Whistleblower and Prevention of Retaliation”to ensure that whistleblowers will be 
free from the threats of retaliation. Please also refer to the Employee Code of Conduct and the 
rules governing complaints and protection against retaliation.

Intranet Bulletin 
Through our intranet bulletin system, we are able to post relevant information such as

and is published every two months. Contents include behind-the-scene reports on company events, 
amateur photography, original comics, travel journals, poetry, essays, ESG column, and workplace 
announcements, it is a medium of creative outlet for our employees.

06.4 Workplace Health and Safety
06.4.1 Health at Compal
 144
Happiness at work and in life
Employee Benefits and Activities
Employees are an important asset to the 
Company so taking care of employees in one 
of our top priorities. Compal not only provides 
employees with various benefits but also hosts 
activities that encourage employees to be 
happy in their work and enjoy the good things 
in life. In addition to subsidies for marriage, 
bereavement, childbirth, emergency assistance, 
and holiday bonuses (gift vouchers), Taipei 
operations also has contracts with HESS, 
O.U.R.S., Kojen Preschool, and Taipei Children 
Welfare Center to provide kindergarten, 
daycare and after-school care services for 
employees with children aged between 2 ~ 12. 
Plants offer employees production bonuses as 
well as marriage, bereavement, travel subsidies 
and birthday gift vouchers. To promote team 
cohesion, we subsidize departmental social 
gatherings, employee birthday parties, and 
sporting competitions that help employees 
find a balance in their work, realize happiness 
at work and enjoyment of life, so that they 
can create even more value and a sense of 
achievement. Each plant plans its own activities 
in accordance with local festivals and demands 
of employees The details of the activities in 
2023 are shown as below:
Flexible Working Hours and Work-Life Balance
All Compal plants around the world offer flex-
time and child/family care leave based on local 
conditions to help employees achieve work-life 
balance and improve their quality of work. All 
global plants also offer suitable breastfeeding 
locations and breaks so that female employees can 
balance their work and child-rearing.
o	 Flexible Working Hours
In Taiwan, employees can choose to start between 
7: 30 AM and 9: 00AM; at the Chengdu and 
Chongqing plants, managers can set their own 
start/finish times to satisfy their attendance 
requirements for the day; at the Brazil plant, 
employees can set their own start/finish times to 
satisfy their attendance requirements for the week.
o	 Part-Time Working Options
In Taiwan, some positions offer employees the 
option of working part-time for the Company. 
Employees in Taiwan and at the Chongqing Plant 
may also apply to work on a part-time basis 
for a certain period of time to meet their family 
obligations.
o	 Breast-Feeding/Lactation Facilities or Benefits
In Taiwan, China, and Vietnam, employees have 
60 minutes of breast-feeding (expressing) time 
each day. If an employee is nursing multiple 
babies, Kunshan Plant offers an additional 30 
minutes per baby, while Chengdu Plant offers an 
Taiwan
Electronic coupons for birthdays, Labor Day, 
Mid-Autumn Festival, and Dragonboat Festival; 
lifestyle and entertainment subsidies; arts & 
literature, marriage, childbirth, bereavement, 
and emergency assistance subsidies; 
scholarships (employee continuing education 
scholarship/dependents education scholarship), 
end of year party, family day, corporate child

talent and comedy show, fun challenges, and

additional 60 minutes of breast-feeding time; in

(expressing) breaks a day at a time of their own 
choosing.
o	 Paid Parental Leave
In Taiwan, primary and secondary caregivers may 
apply for up to 6 months of childcare leave and 
receive a childcare stipend in accordance with 
government regulations. Primary and secondary 
caregivers at Kunshan, Chengdong, Chengdu, 
and Nanjing plants are entitled to 10 days of 
paid parental leave annually until their children 
reach the age of three; in Vietnam, employees are 
entitled to 1 hour of paid childcare leave each day; 
in Brazil, the primary and secondary caregivers are 
entitled to 20 days of paid childcare leave a year.
o	 Paid Family or Care Leave
In Taiwan, employees are entitled to 3 days of paid 
companionship leave. Managers also receive an 
additional 7 days of paid family leave. Employees at 
the Kunshan, Chengdong and Nanjing plants who 
are the only-child are entitled to 5 days of paid 
nursing leave a year if their parents are hospitalized 
and over 60 years old.
o	 Remote Working Plan
Employees in Taiwan and at the Chongqing Plant 
may apply to work remotely if they are unable to 
commute due to special circumstances
Note: Managers refer to employees above the grade 
of section manager.

Employee Assistance Program (EAP) was introduced by Compal 
in 2019. Professional external consultants work with Compal to 
provide employees with advice on topics such as work, family, 
interpersonal relations, physical and mental wellbeing, mental 
illness, finance, legal studies and management. Employees are 
provided with a wide range of support that safeguards their 
physical and mental wellbeing, and sustainable talent. In 2023, 
12 EAP-themed seminars with a total duration of 47 hours were 
held to help employees and supervisors reduce the obstacle to 
communication and interaction. The meeting aimed to open 
communications regarding work and management so pave the 
way for ground solutions.
Phase 1 - Usage statistics for consultants hotline: 1,355 times
Phase 2- Individual query statistics
In 2023,there were 176 individual consultations and the cumulative duration was 182 hours for the year.

 146
Employee Health Management
Compal organizes regular health check-ups and set up 
infirmaries in Taipei and Pingzhen to provide health services 
including: emergency treatment and physician consultations. 
The management platform effectively tracks the health status 
of employees. By teaching preventive medicine concepts, 
conveying proper health information and providing health 
management and care, health concepts are introduced to 
families and expanding the benefits of health promotion.
Health Examination
Health check-ups provides health information that can be 
used to realize the goal of preventive medicine through 
prevention and improvement. A health exam is arranged 
for all employees every two years based on the nature of 
their work and working environment at the plant. On top of 
statutorily required items, the Company also offers subsidies 
for more common diseases. Employees can choose optional 
exams based on their own health and family history. With 
dissemination and regular reminders, 90.1% of employees in 
Taiwan and overseas finished health check-ups in 2023.
Health Care
The Company has established health plans to reduce risk and 
prevent illness. We also provide health protection for special 
subjects as well as occupational prevention, identification and 
investigation in accordance with Ministry of Labor regulations. 
These help ensure the physical and mental well-being of 
employees, and provide them with support.
Management of Health Promotion Platform: (Taiwan only)
All plants in Taiwan have set up a health promotion platform 
for managing and supporting employee health requirements. 
The platform integrates health-related information services so 
that nurses can effectively manage employee health, identify 
and assess health risks, and provide the corresponding 
support and assistance. Employees can use the platform as 
well to query about health check-up information and register 
for services/activities, providing convenient health services.
Health examination reports are classified into Level 1,Level 2,Level 3,and Moderate-to-High Cardiovascular Risk 
Group for management. Health education and guidance is provided to those in the Moderate-to-High Cardio-
vascular Group, Level 3 (Three Highs), and Level 2 (Hypertension/High Blood Sugar) categories. Employees with 
significant anomalies are assessed by physicians then provided with support and follow-up.
o	 Health management was achieved for 94.6% of employees in the moderate-to-high risk group for cardiovas-
cular disease.
o	 100% implementation rate of maternal labor health protection with follow-up and management for over 70%.
o	 Musculo-skeletal symptoms are periodically examined in conjunction with routine operational health exams.
o	 Number of physician consultations and health education sessions: 960 times
o	 Clinic assistance: 485 times
1. Health exam report: Health exams are sorted with high-risk employees prioritized for health guidance. Those 
in the moderate-to-high risk group for cardiovascular disease undergo a stress overload scale assessment to 
determine how their workload affects their health.
2. Implementation of MOL protective measures: 
(1).	 Maternal Health Protection Program.
(2).	 Ergonomic Hazard Prevention Program.
(3).	 Prevention of Illness Triggered by Abnormal Workload Program.

Employee Health Promotion
The organizing of health activities help to build 
health awareness, cultivate a healthy lifestyle, 
promote teamwork and cohesion, and reduce 
lifestyle-related health problems. Employees 
are also given a better understanding of their 
own physical and mental condition so they can 
adjust their lifestyle, maintain healthy habits, 
and stay in a sound condition. A total of 15 
activities were organized in 2023.
Blood Donation
Uphold the spirit of helping others to help 
yourself so that everyone can have the 
opportunity to practice philanthropy and 
spread the message of compassion.This year, 
3 sessions were held with 330 participants. 
125,750 cc of blood was donated.
Health Seminars
5 seminars were held this year. The contents 
were quite rich and diverse. They also covered 
how to look after common care problems, diet 
of dining out tips, and aromatherapy. Online 
classes were concurrently held at Pingzhen 
plant. Employees unable to attend in person 
were able to also take part in learning more 
about health. A total of 281 people took part.
Health Activities
To encourage employees to exercise regularly for 
physical health and comfort, we hosted 3 sporting 
events and provided year-round masseuse 
services. Total participation was 2,146. The healthy 
walking activity was voluntary. We providegd 
participants health information every week and 
tracked voluntary walking status through step 
counts reported by participants. Over 80.2% of 
the participants walked more than 7,000 steps in 
average a day during the event. The satisfaction 
survey of the event showed that percentage of 
participants walked more than 7,000 steps in 
average a day increased from 23.7% to 78.9%. 
Also, 99% of participants continue walking as a 
habit after the event. (Survey response rate: 76%).
Disease Prevention
Vaccinations and cancer screenings help with 
early detection of potential health problems and 
enhance employee health awareness.
In 2023,a total of 196 people participated in three 
flu vaccination and cancer screening events.

Participation in team competitions not only strengthen physical constitution and health but also 
fosters greater trust and cooperation between team members. These translate into greater team 
cohesion and cooperation.
During 2023, Taiwan hosted team competitions for badminton, bubble football and arcade games. 
277 people took part in ball sports competitions. At the same time, a variety of sports clubs have 
also been set up to satisfy the diverse interests/needs of employees and to provide them with more 
options. The organizing of small sports clubs for badminton, basketball, boxercise, fitness yoga, and 
ballet body sculpting helped to cultivate an atmosphere of healthy living.
The Company offers maternal support and care so that employees can concentrate fully on 
looking after newborns, achieve a balance between work and family, and cultivate a family-
friendly workplace. Low birth-rates and high stress today mean that we place even greater 
emphasis on maternal care and stress counseling. The Company strives to look after our 
maternal employees in every way so they can feel secure and continue developing their careers. 
EAP conducted by professional bodies help employees eliminate sources of stress and embark 
on a better life.
Maternal Services and Care in Taiwan
A.	 Pre- and post-natal work hazard assessments (incl. investigation physical hazards, human 
factor hazards, stress and personal health assessments) are conducted for employees. In-
person consultations are arranged if necessary to provide health guidance and advice during 
pregnancy and breast-feeding.
B.	 Preventive action is taken if any hazards to maternal health are identified by the assessment 
and their work is adjusted if necessary.
C.	 Establishment of lactation room.
D.	 Hosting of female cancer screening (Pap smear/ MAMMOGRAPHY).
E.	 Distribution of health education information on child-rearing each month.
F.	 Free parking spaces for pregnant women are provided at Taoyuan plant and Linkou.
G.	 Childbirth bonuses.

CHAPTER

To provide employees sound development in their careers and 
realize a physiological and psychological well-being workplace, 
we began conducting the Employee Happiness Survey in 2022. 
The targets and results of related investigations and analyses 
are also published. To ensure the investigation and analysis 
findings can be compared horizontally (between groups/units) 
and vertically (between years), the survey’s structure, questions 
and analytical methods all adhered to consistent principles. 
The questions are designed using published academic 
papers/periodicals. Comparative analysis is also conducted 
for discrepancies between groups to further enhance the 
effectiveness of the survey.
Survey Contents and Scale: 
In this survey, the survey questions are divided into four 
indicators including “Happiness”, “Purpose”, “Satisfaction”and 
“Stress”. The four indicators were used to analyze employee 
happiness at work. Survey scoring scale was divided into: 
Strongly Disagree, Disagree, Acceptable, Agree, and Strongly 
Agree. The corresponding scores ranged from 1 for Strongly 
Disagree to 5 for Strongly Agree. There are 20 questions and the 
total score is out of 100.
Survey Outcome
In 2023, average score from the Employee Well-Being Survey 
was 72.92. This time, we recovered 23,386 survey responses 
and received 23,290 valid responses. The effective recovery rate 
was 99.6%. The recovery rate for valid responses in each survey 
has been set as over 85% to ensure the confidence interval and 
relevance of the statistical analysis results.
Through the analysis of related projects, the Company is 
able to monitor the current happiness of employees and set 
improvement targets for next year (the target for 2024 is set as 
74). The corresponding improvements were then conducted as 
planned. For improvement plans aimed at employee happiness, 
the Company selected the three topics with the lowest 
satisfaction from the survey findings for in-depth analysis to 
identify the groups that people with low satisfaction belong to 
(married or single, male or female). Improvement suggestions 
are then proposed to review and follow-up. These embodied the 
importance of employee suggestions to the Company, and the 
commitment to building a happy and sound workplace.

6.4.2 Occupational Health and Safety
 150
Occupational Safety Policy, Internal Culture
Occupational Safety and Health Management 
System Certification
Occupational Safety and Health Committee 
Compal knows that employees, contractors, suppliers and 
workers are all important assets in the sustainable development 
of a company. Compliance with Occupational Safety and Health 
Act and other applicable requirements is therefore mandated 
during the development, testing, and mass production of 
company products. We also hope that all employees can grow 
in a safe working environment. We have therefore defined an 
Environmental Safety and Health Policy (ESH Policy), established 
an Occupational Safety Management System, regularly 
host disaster prevention and firefighting drills, promote 
environmental safety training, and provide employees with 
places to relax physically and mentally outside of work. By 
boosting the physical and mental satisfaction of employees, 
we can prevent occupational injuries due to unsafe behavior, 
environment and equipment, and reduce the likelihood of 
absenteeism to give employees peace of mind at work and a 
healthy lifestyle.
Compal Environmental Safety and Health Policy
To protect the occupational safety of employees at work, we 
have not only established the Environmental Safety and Health 
Policy but also established relevant procedures and documents 
of the “Occupational Safety and Health Management” at each 
plant site in order to rigorously control details of each work 
place. We also require each plant to obtain ISO45001: 2018 
certification to ensure that all employees and workers stationed 
at the plant are not exposed to danger or injured due to 
improper procedures at work. The certification encompasses 
occupational hazard identification, emergency response 
measures, contractor management etc. Through procedural 
document control and repeated PDCA (Plan-Do-Check-Act) 
verification cycles, employee work safety can be enforced. 
The occupational safety and health management system is 
applicable to all working personnel (including contractor 
personnel) at the plant. Plants are also required to conduct 
proper education and training. 
An Occupational Safety and Health Committee has been 
established by Compal Taiwan in accordance with the law. 
Overseas plants hold regular meetings under the occupational 
safety and health management system. The OSH Committee 
is made up of management and employee representatives. 
Employee representatives speak for all employees and engage 
with the management on occupational safety matters to facilitate 
communication and consultation between company departments, 
throughout the company hierarchy, and relevant external 
units/bodies, as well as ensure a safe working environment for 
employees.
We explicitly specify the responsibilities of the management 
and employee representatives according to the management 
of the “Environmental and Occupational Health and Safety 
Handbook”, “Environmental and Occupational Health and Safety 
Policy Establishment Policy”, “Environmental and Occupational 
Health and Safety Internal Audit Management Procedures” of 
the plant sites, and through the procedures of “Environmental 
Safety Improvement Communication Procedures. ”Employee 
representatives shall participate in the development and review of 
safety and health policies and relevant procedures.
Prior to the meeting, if any unit has doubts or specific 
recommendations on the current method, it can be submitted 
to relevant units, such as the Occupational Safety Office. After 
the receiving unit receives the notice, the “Environmental Safety 
Improvement Recommendation Form” is completed in order 
to feed back issues to relevant units, executing unit, thereby 
facilitating swift resolution of such issues. If such issue cannot be 
resolved timely, it will be discussed in the committee meeting.

Frequency and Agenda of OHS Committee Meetings in Each Region
Responsibilities of Committee Members
OSH meetings are convened in Taiwan in accordance with Article 12 of the Regulations 
Governing Occupational Safety and Health on a quarterly basis. The agenda includes but 
is not limited to the following: 
Coordination and making of recommendations on the OSH management plan; review 
of health management, occupational disease prevention, and health promoting matters; 
review of OSH proposals; review of occupational disaster investigation reports and ep-
idemic prevention plans.
The following matters are discussed at OSH meetings convened by overseas plants in 
accordance with the OSH management system requirements: 
Signing of Safe Responsibility Agreement and environmental safety KPI, self-assessment 
on safe production standardization, as well as the joint formulation of environmental 
safety policies, goals, and proposals, and epidemic prevention planning.
Note: Plants with no disclosures will host ad hoc meetings in some other manner.
o	 Approve publication of management system documents, and responsible for the decision making of the 
establishment, completeness and operation maintenance of management system of the company.
o	 Determine environmental directives and environmental goals, ensuring alignment with the company’s 
overall objectives.
o	 Direct the management level to conduct reviews, approve and review plans; direct the environmental and 
occupational health and safety goal achievement status review etc.
Duties for execution include but not limited to the following: 
o	 Internal and external environmental safety communication and handling, execution of relevant responsibili-
ties; routine environmental safety management. Emergency response organization and coordination.
o	 Responsible for the environment and occupational health and safety management goals, subject matters 
and management solution establishment and implementation for the department. 
o	 Manage documents and records of the department; control of environmental and occupational health and 
safety system documents, records.
o	 Propose corrective and preventive measures for violations and execution of other matters.

Occupational Hazard Identification and Risk Assessment
Safety and Health Hazardous Risk Identification, 
Assessment and Control Operation Process
The prevention of occupational injuries depends on protecting the 
physical health and safety of employees as well as the prevention 
and mitigation of impact OSH impacts. Hazard identification and 
risk assessment is conducted by Compal on employee work areas 
and any hazard factors on the shop floor closely monitored to 
ensure their impact on employees is minimized. The scope of 
hazard identification and risk assessment include all health and 
safety hazards that may affect the inside and outside of the plant, 
but also include routine and non-routine activities, all personnel 
(including contractors and visitors) entering the plant, and 
outside contractors in the workplace. OSH hazard identification 
and risk assessments are conducted by the relevant task force 
(identification team). Moderate/high-risk or urgent hazards from 
the assessment findings are reported to the management review 
committee. The level of risk is then used to formulate the priority 
action plan for the year as well as devise the corresponding 
targets, specifications and management plans.
At the Pingzheng Plant in Taiwan for an example, risk assessment 
taskforce conducts annual hazard identifications or as necessary 
in accordance with the “Safety and Health Hazard Identification 
Form. ”The result is recorded in the “Risk Assessment Form” to 
serve as a basis for policy formulation and hazard management. 
Management review meeting is convened periodically, and the 
promotion taskforce conducts discussion, revision and approval 
on the newly identified risks. For risks already identified and 
content requiring revision, revision is further made. The risk level 
standard and control are revised annually to align with corporate 
requirements.
The ISO 45001 OSH management system is strictly enforced by 
plants in China as well. The LEC method for hazard assessment 
of working conditions is conducted in accordance with the 
“Hazard Management Control Procedure” to identify and assess 
OSH hazards within the scope of the Company, assess the level 
of risk and identify major hazards so that they can be effectively 
controlled.

Frequency of occurrence
Frequency is classified into the number of occurrence for a 
period of above 5 years, within 5 years, 1 year, less than 1 
year etc. 
Severity
It is classified according to the nature of severity of no 
obvious hazard, possibly leading to medical treatment needs, 
causing disability, death etc.
Risk weight
 Non-routine work X Accidents once occurred X (1 - current 
control effect*))
Note: With effective equipment protection, operation control 
and warning signs, personnel and property loss and hazard are 
reduced
Risks are identified by the above risk assessment process and 
moderate-to-high hazard factors closely monitored so that 
the vision and goal of reduction in occupational disasters can 
be realized. Safe Working Environment
Risk Assessment Form Score 
= Frequency of Occurrence x Severity x Risk weight

1. 	A hazard score between 70-160 represents a significant hazard that 
requirements timely remediation.
2. 	A hazard score between 160-320 represents a high-risk environment where 
remedial action must be taken immediately.
3. 	A hazard score above 320 indicates a very dangerous environment that 
requires immediate rectification.
3. 	Use and storage of chemicals: Improper storage of chemicals can lead to spills and 
fire; improper use can lead to the eyes being sprayed, skin contact, and dissipation of 
odors.
(a) Education and training for supervisors and operators.
(b) Execute the emergency preparation and response management procedure in an 
emergency. 
(c) SDS and protective gear must be provided on the shop floor.
(d) Personnel that need to enter the organic solvents plant room are governed by the 
Hazardous Chemical Safety Management Implementation Rules. The custodian for 
the organic solvent plant room must be notified to provide on-site supervision.
4. Cafeteria Management: Staff dining (accidental injuries such as crowding), improper 
management and control of ingredients and site increase risk of contamination and 
food poisoning; management of cafeteria equipment.
(a) Staggering of employee dining times in accordance with the Cafeteria Operation 
Management Regulations. 
(b) In response to the COVID-19 pandemic, cafeteria implemented centralized man-
agement of temperature readings for cafeteria staff, disinfection, provision of 
gloves and masks, and display of posters; if an employee shows sign of poisoning 
they must be sent to the infirmary for emergency treatment then transported to a 
regular hospital as soon as possible. 
(c) Follow instruction manual during equipment operations and pay attention to 
electrical safety during use. 
(d) Beware of slipper surface signs should be placed when the cafeteria is being 
cleaned. Contract cleaning personnel should wear non-slip foootwear and practice 
wet/dry separation.
5. Employee commutes and driving of non-motorized vehicles within the plant: Traffic 
accidents due to excessive vehicles speed.
(a) Education and awareness enhanced with traffic police stationed at key intersections 
during commuter hours to prevent accidents.
(b) Helmets should be worn when non-motorized vehicles are entering or leaving the 
premises. Cyclists should slow down.
1. 	Operation of production equipment: Noise generated by machine operation, 
improper operation, and personnel injury due to equipment malfunction.
(a) Operators undergo periodic education and training. They must also follow 
the operating procedures religiously. 
(b) Annual monitoring in n accordance with the MP027 Control Measures for 
Environmental Monitoring and Measurement
2. 	Office and production activities: Fires caused by improper operation of ap-
pliances and equipment; viral infections, computer radiation, forced posture, 
and visual fatigue. 
(a) Establish emergency response team and have Plant Affairs conduct and 
log monthly inspections of emergency response facilities; Regular fire 
safety drills are held by ESH to boost employee awareness on evacua-
tions. 
(b) Due to the COVID-19 pandemic, the Company set up an emergency 
resposne team for epidemic prevention and put up epidemic information 
posters; new hires and those completed two years of service undergo 
health exams once every two years organized by administrative services. 
(c) Execute emergency response plan and monitor the surrounding environ-
ment. 
(d) Periodic education on disaease prevention. 
(e) Reduce unnecessary use of computers and set up screensaver sleep func-
tions to reduce computer radiation. 
(f) A Ten-minute break every two hours to alleviate fatigue.

Emergency Response Measures and Occupational Disaster Investigation
Each plant area is equipped with Emergency Preparedness and Response 
Measures, and the documents explain in detail the “Risk Description”, “Emergency 
Organization and Responsibility”, “Prevention and Internal Notification”, 
“Emergency Response”, “External Information Release”, “Follow-up Treatment”, 
etc., and the handling procedures of various risks are listed in detail.
In the event of any injuries due to occupational or natural disasters at a Compal 
plant, the unit involved must follow procedure and notify the head of the unit 
and other relevant units in accordance with the OSH management system. 
An investigation form must also be filled out to activate the investigation 
mechanism. An occupational disaster investigation should cover a minimum of 
two areas, namely the environment (environment and equipment configuration, 
medium of injury, OSH measures, location of disaster), people (how the disaster 
happened and rescue efforts, the state of the victim at the time, normal 
or routine operating procedures/methods, whether there were witnesses, 
description of the situation and opinions). Handling of traffic accidents: If 
a vehicle transporting Compal products is involved in an accident off-site, 
this should be reported to its transportation company immediately and the 
Occupational Safety Office notified as well. If there is any damage or injury to the 
vehicle or personnel, the local police should be notified. Handling of accident 
injuries (including death, disability injury, minor injury, and traffic accident injury 
when commuting): The direct supervisor should be notified first and then the 
involved individual taken to hospital for examination and first-aid. The head 
of the involved unit must notify the Occupational Safety Office within 3 hours 
no matter how light or severe the injury. In Taiwan, the occupational disaster 
statistics are compiled on a monthly basis and reported online to the local 
inspection mechanism by the Occupational Safety Office in accordance with 
regulations. A detailed reporting process is executed according to the procedural 
documents.
According to regulations, all plants of Compal only sign cooperation contracts 
with legitimate Human Resource agency companies, and all of the hired security, 
kitchen, cleaning personnel etc. shall be protected by the contract.
In case where the workers are subject to accidents, the reports to their direct 
team leader or management personnel are made first, following which the 
plant supervisor shall conduct a field confirmation, in order to assist the injured 
personnel with the hospital treatment and insurance claim.

 155
Environmental Safety in the Workplace 
Occupational Safety and Health Education & Training
Employee Absentee Rate
Access Control Implementation
To comply with the ISMS (Information Security Management 
System) regulations, employees are required to wear 
employee identification badges at all time in the plant site for 
identification. The access card system at each entrance and exit 
controls personnel’s access authority. For clients, suppliers, and 
other visitors, a security system is used to record the time of 
visit, the number of visitors, and regulate the areas and time 
open to visitors. Compal’s security personnel work 24 hours a 
day to control entry of personnel and objects, perform safety 
inspections day and night inside and outside plants, monitor 
the presence of visitors and overtime workers, check incoming/
outgoing vehicles, and perform traffic control.
Workplace Environmental Monitoring
To provide a safe workplace and community for our staff and 
residents, each plant is staffed with a unit responsible for 
routine inspection and maintenance, as well as identifying 
hazardous factors in the work environment. For example: 
Transportation and electrical safety measures, safety inspection 
measures, drinking water testing, emergency lighting testing, 
smoke detector testing, and firefighting equipment inspection. 
Environmental monitoring in the workplace is arranged by each 
plant twice a year to measure the chemicals present or used on-
site. Testing covers office illumination, CO2 concentration, and 
chemical monitoring.
OSH-Compliance in Procurement Management
To ensure a safe and healthy environment for employees, the 
procurement of all machinery, equipment, raw materials and 
personal protection equipment used by the Company, as well 
as all building and construction work must stipulate supplier 
or contractor compliance with laws, regulations, and OHS 
specifications. Compliance must be verified during acceptance 
and before start of construction to reduce employee exposure 
to OSH hazards in the environment.
Labor Safety Drills and Education
Compal implements employee safety educational training 
courses to allow employees to understand the safety of 
the plant site and possible hazardous risks. In addition, the 
Company also assist employees to understand the disaster level 
and response measures, escape moving lines etc. according to 
the “Emergency Response Measure Management Procedures” 
and no disciplinary actions are imposed on employees leaving 
works due to emergency evacuationNote. In addition, we 
cooperate with the regional fire department to implement fire 
prevention training and annual fire education. We designed 
teaching materials on the proper response to fire, storms, 
flooding and earthquakes for online e-learning or physical 
classes. Employees must also sit an exam after the course 
and pass to complete the training. To help raise employee 
awareness on everyday disaster prevention concepts, the 
Company conducts live exercise on fire, the most common type 
of disaster, to teach employees what actions to take and what 
to watch out for. Fire drills are conducted every year at all plants 
worldwide and posted on the intranet for employees to view. 
The fire drills of the R&D Center and each plant are held in 
compliance with the times and hours of the law and regulation. 
Note: In accordance of “Occupational Safety and Health Act” 
Article 18 : When there is a concern of a potential imminent 
danger at a workplace, the employers or people responsible 
for the worksite shall immediately issue orders to halt work 
and withdraw laborers to a safe location. The employers shall 
not dismiss, reassign, not pay wages for the period of work on 
halt, or otherwise impose unfavorably treatment on laborers 
taking actions prescribed in the preceding paragraph. Although 
overseas factories are not regulated by Taiwanese laws, their 
internal regulations are based on the requirements verified by 
the Taiwanese factories and occupational safety and health 
management systems as a reference template.
Compal are committed to establishing and maintaining a 
safe and healthy workplace environment to reduce employee 
absentee due to illness and injuries, thereby achieving stable 
organizational productivity.
2023 Target: 2% absentee rate with 100% global coverage. 	
(Target achieved)
Absentee Rate from 2020 to 2023
Notes: 
(1) Absentee rate calculations does not include leave that was 
planned by employees or approved in advance including national 
public holidays, maternity leave, paternity leave, special leave, and 
annual travel leave; all other leave applications due to employee 
injury, illness, or personal reasons included in the calculation. 
These include: work-related injury leave, case leave, sick leave, 
maternity leave, abortion leave, and menstrual leave.
(2) Absentee rate equation: No. of absentee days from global 
employees / No. of days worked by global employees during the 
accounting period x 100%
(3) COVID-19 led to strict restrictions in of the Company’s regions 
in 2022. Due to regional quarantine policies in each region, the 
absentee rate was somewhat higher than the previous years.

Occupational Safety Management Procedures
Resident personnel include temporary employees, interns, 
stationed personnel (typically refer to security guards, cafeteria 
personnel etc.). Compal ensures a safe and healthy working 
environment for all resident personnel and contracts on-site in 
accordance with the OSH management system, OSH Act (Article 
23), OSH Management Regulations (Article 12-2) and local 
regulations in Brazil.

07. Social Engagement
 158
Key Performance
o	 In 2023,Compal took part in social engagement a total of 4,533 participants (*including 
216 college reading volunteers sponsored by Compal) and total investment amounted to 
NT$27,229,020. There were 75,163 beneficiaries in total.
o	 Compal was presented with the “Social Education Contribution Awards - Group Award”by the 
Ministry of Education, “Social Education Contribution Award - Group Award”by the Education 
Bureau of Kaohsiung City Government, and the “Social Service Awards - Group Award”by the 
Library Association of the R.O.C. (Taiwan).
o	 The first Compal “Joyful Reading Area”program was established at the Mituo Branch of 
Kaohsiung Public Library by Compal. In the 4th year of the program, the “ESG Reading 
Program”for the remote villages was launched in partnership with Kaohsiung Public Library to 
help local communities in the Liugui Branch, Tianliao Branch, Jiashen Branch, and Mituo Park 
Branch. A total of 16,960 local students and residents benefited.
o	 Compal donated 235 wireless desk lamps to help disadvantaged schoolchildren with learning at 
home. We have helped 485 students with their studies over two years so far.
o	 Emphasis on the environmental education of native species and wetland conservation by hosting 
5 mangrove environmental education sessions. A total of 446 Compal employees, their families 
and elementary school students took part in the mangrove wetland ecological conservation 
course and on-site visit.
o	 NT$ 8,501,150 invested so far towards GOLF alliance for the cultivation of professional talent.
o	 Compal donated NT$10 million to disaster relief after the Hualien Earthquake in 2024. The Kinpo 
Group donated NT$20 million.

07.1 Social Care - Influence
 159
07.1 Social Care - Influence
Compal Social Inclusion Vision: Create a society of “new 
happiness”through a “caring”enterprise by leverage the 
spirit of compassion and energy in every Compal employee.
Compal has long invested in innovative R&D and digital 
technology products to better human life. We have been 
actively investing in smart healthcare in recent years 
as well so that all human beings and other species on 
Earth can live in peace and happiness. Employees are 
encouraged to contribute their strengths and volunteer. 
Emphasis is placed on improving the quality of learning 
for disadvantaged students, bridging the rural-urban gap 
in education, promoting rural community development, 
and sustainable environment and ecology. We hope that 
everyone can have the power to use knowledge in a 
diverse and inclusive ways. We support the development 
that upholds regional characteristics while also improving 
the international competitiveness of individuals and 
communities.
The combined powers of Compal employees are 
channeled through Hsu Chauing Social Welfare 
Foundation, group subsidiaries, affiliates, customers and 
supply chain partners to fill society with the energy of 
happiness through “corporate philanthropy.”Create a 
society of “new happiness”through a “caring”enterprise 
by leveraging the spirit of compassion and energy in 
every Compal employee. Realize the sustainability mission 
of “giving back to society.”
To eliminate hunger and poverty, Compal promotes 
quality education and initiatives. We enforce climate 
change mitigation and adaptation policies in order to 
realize the 17 UN Sustainable Development Goals (SDGs) 
by 2030 and the target of net zero carbon emissions by 
2050. We work together with citizens of the planet to 
create an inclusive society. We strive to a peaceful society 
based on respect, fairness, and inclusivity.
Social Inclusion - Sustainability Strategy:
1. Digital transformation and bridging of the education gap.
2. Conservation of cultural heritage and respect for cultural diversity.
3. Emphasis on environmental sustainability and support for joint initiatives.
4. Life and health care, caring for the disadvantaged.
5. Promotion of care services and encouragement of volunteer contribution.

7.3.1 Innovation and Quality Education
 171

::: Appendixes
::: Introduction to the Sustainability Report    ::: 2023 Sustainability Accolades    ::: Letters From the Executive Officers    01 About Compal    
02 Compal and Stakeholders    03 Corporate Governance    04 Sustainable Products    05 Climate Change and GHG Management    
06 Inclusive Growth    07 Social Engagement / 07.3 Public Welfare Practice at Compal    08 Sustainability Partners    ::: Appendixes
Rapid advances in technology and digital innovation has made closing the gap 
in teachers and educational resources between the city and countryside all but 
impossible.
Compal leveraged the Group’s innovative technologies and expertise in product 
R&D to assist the disadvantaged in society. We supported initiatives launched 
by the Group’s Hsu Chauing Social Welfare Charity Foundation to raise the 
quality of education for schoolchildren. We believe in the importance of national 
character education and the practice of altruistic values. We encourage students 
to “learn by doing, think while learning”to strengthen the application of pro-
fessional knowledge, and help students from disadvantaged families in society 
learn and grow so that they can show their zest for life, practice charity and 
compassion, and play an active role in social and national affairs.
o Encouraged employees to participate in social care and volunteering services 
- Mobilize the power of businesses, corporate volunteers, and student 
volunteers to serve the community and engage in social care together.
o Helped raise the quality of education for schoolchildren and residents in rural 
communities.
o Collaborative charity projects by the Group’s Hsu Chauing Social Welfare 
Charity Foundation
o Industry-university charity projects
o Industry-government-university charity projects
1. 5th year of Compal x FJU Kangaroo Project (2019~2023)
2. Compal Reading Volunteer Program 2007~2023 (16th year)
3. Donation of wireless desk lamps and digital devices by Compal 
“Good Reading Project”, and support for “Bilingual Policy”and 
“Maker Education Project”

o	 Partner

quality of education, quality of life, and learning ability.
o	 Implementation

team rapport, sportsmanship, and regular exercise.
4. Organizing of family day and career experience events, as well as development of courses on ethics 
and life education, gender equality, identifying disinformation online, and community cultural education.

well as establish counseling and companionship services for younger and older students.
6. Training of corporate volunteers on community service, and collaboration with the FJU student 
volunteer team to share love and compassion.

Community services at Mustard Service Garden in Fengshan, Kaohsiung, and Double A Plus Love Center as well as in-person 
tutoring by university student volunteers were added to the “Kangaroo Project” in 2023. The “Fu-Hsing Learning Family Day” 
was hosted for the schoolchildren at Fu-Hsing School of Martial Arts in Miaoli for life education on self-management and 
division of labor. Children with sporting talent were also taught how to manage their own physical condition and prevent 
sports injury to expand their future career options. University student mentors continued to provide in-person mentoring and 
companionship services for schoolchildren at Dayuan in Taoyuan and Quaker Shulin Church in Huilong. The in-person course 
used adaptive teaching to give students the opportunity to learn and rebuild their self-confidence. Tailoring the teaching to 
the student’s actual ability ensured that every child possessed basic learning ability and initiative.

o	 Partner
The Compal Reading Volunteer Program was conducted in partnership with student volunteer clubs from 
11 universities including National Taiwan Normal University, National Taiwan University of Science and 
Technology, Takming University of Science and Technology, Kun Shan University, National Yunlin University 
of Science and Technology, Fooyin University, National Kinmen University, and Taipei Medical University in 
2023.
o	 Beneficiary Units
Nearby schools including Ruimei Township Elementary School (Hualien), Bochun Elementary School and 
Jinding Elementary School (Kinmen), Tuku Elementary School and Yangming Elementary School in Lunbei 
Township (Yunlin), Kunshan Elementary school and Dawan Elementary School (Tainan), as well as Siwan 
Village community near Kun Shan University; P’uma Elementary School and Daguan Village (Taichung), 
Chihshan Junior High School (Taitung), Tanan Elementary School in Xinyi Township (Nantou County), 
Zhongtai Community in Wulai Township (New Taipei CIty), Zhongzhi Taiwan Presbyterian Church, as well as 
Jingxin Elementary School and Yutang Elementary School in Chiangrai Village, Thailand.
o	 Long-term goal
Promotion of reading education in rural schools and communities, environmental education, promotion of 
SDGs. Assist with volunteer training and delivery of community and mentoring services.
o	 Implementation
1. 	Promotion of local community services and international 
volunteer services. Encourage university volunteer clubs to 
conduct grassroots education based on local requirements, 
promotion of SDGs and long-term community heritage 
support projects.
2. 	Provide greater scope and depth for volunteering by 
university students so they can put their personal skills 
to good use. Develop diverse course activities so that 
participating volunteers can practice empathy, communicate 
with schoolchildren, and grow through mutual understanding.
3. 	Promotion of reading education to bridge the gap in rural 
education to help students improve their studies, digital 
information, and character education for balance in the Six 
Ways of Life. Addition of critical thinking and teamwork.
4. 	Strong emphasis placed on sustainability, promotion of 
environmental awareness and plastic reduction, and engaging 
in individual sustainability action to prepare for natural 
disasters caused by climate change.

06 Inclusive Growth    07 Social Engagement / 07.3 Public Welfare Practice at Compal    08 Sustainability Partners    ::: Appendixes
Declining birth rates across the world are making it difficult for businesses to find 
the people they need. To bridge the urban-rural divide in quality of education for 
schoolchildren, youths are provide with suitable professional training to enhance 
their professional skills.
Schoolchildren from disadvantaged families were given assistance and professional 
instruction to put their talents to good use.
Compal leveraged the Group’s innovative technologies and expertise in product 
R&D to assist the disadvantaged in society. We supported initiatives launched by 
the Group’s Hsu Chauing Social Welfare Charity Foundation to raise the quality of 
education for schoolchildren. We also cooperated with government and Ministry of 
Education outreach projects for helping disadvantaged families and schoolchildren 
in society.
o Encouraged employees to participate in care and volunteer activities on their own 
initiative.
o Helped raise the quality of education for schoolchildren and residents in rural 
communities.
o Collaborative charity projects by the Group’s Hsu Chauing Social Welfare Charity 
Foundation
o Industry-university charity projects
o Industry-government-university charity projects
1. 	Employees took part in Compal and Hsu Chauing 
Social Welfare Charity Foundation’s “Dream Come 
True Program” for the 12th year (2012-2023)
2. 	Gap of Learning and Field (GOLF) (2018-2023, 4th 
year), global talent cultivation
3. 	The Brazil plant R&D fund donation
The Brazil plant donated BRL 2,000, 000 to the CEA 
high school student R&D fund again in 2023 to support 
technology education courses (integrated of electronics, 
data science, electro-mechanics) for 506 disadvantaged 
youths. Software development training was also provided 
for students from the 25 UFAC Amazon Academy to improve 
the local economy. Industrial 4.0 training was provided for 
56 people from the Renbaohe Community. All received 
certification as automation system analyst.

Compal and Hsu Chauing Social Welfare Charity Foundation’s 
“Dream Come True Program” for the 12th year
Outcomes
1. In 2023,268 Compal employees donated NT$2,748,700 to promote the “Dream Come True 
Program” on their own initiative. Hsu Chauing Social Welfare Charity Foundation donated NT$5,040, 
277 to provide 3,261 disadvantaged schoolchildren throughout Taiwan with talent training and help 
them realize their potential.
2. Hsu Chauing Social Welfare Charity Foundation has invested NT$19,365,418 in the “Dream Come 
True Program” since 2012. 16,145 schoolchildren have benefited as a result.	
3. Hsu Chauing Social Welfare Charity Foundation continued to help schools set up 116 “Hsu 
Chauing Disadvantaged Children Talent Classes”, and provided professional instruction for 3,525 
schoolchildren. Around 165,500 people have so far benefited between 2012~2023.
4. Compal continued to sponsored overseas competition and training by the national aerobics 
champion Lian-jun Wei from National Taiwan Sport University. Wei won the men’s single gold medal 
at the 2023 FIG Aerobic Gymnastics World Championships in Portugal.

to good use, and provide opportunity to 
reverse the future through quality education.

“Dream Come True Program” to help with the 
talent development of disadvantaged children 
and promote healthy spiritual growth.

General Association of Chinese Culture, Lienchiang 
County Government
o	 Beneficiary Units
More than 20, 000 local Matsu residents and visiting 
members of the public.
o	 Long-term goal

/ performances, paintings, performing arts, and

teams, 70 spectacular artworks, 21 performances, and 
7 styles of co-branded merchandise. The activities 
were expanded to the four townships / five islands 
as well. The contrast between the natural beauty of 
Matsu and the artworks created new local attractions.
2. We hope to stimulate the economy on the 
offshore islands as well as provide more business and 
employment opportunities.

7.3.4 Environmental and Ocean Conservation
Taiwan is an island country so the effects of climate change will be even more 
acute. Joining the rest of the planet in reducing the burden on the planet by 
achieving the Net Zero by 2050 target. Global climate change risk management, 
food and energy shortages, environmental pollution, and the effect of biodiversi-
ty on wetland conservation! 
Popularization of climate change education, collaborate with environmental 
NGOs and other businesses to carry out environmental initiatives.
Encourage Compal employees as well as their families and friends to participate 
in environmental education courses and environmental protection actions. Em-
phasize the importance of habitat ecology and marine conservation on the local 
natural environment.
o Encouraged employees to participate in energy conservation and environmen-
tal volunteering activities on their own initiative.
o Continue to support the UN 30 (ocean) x 30 (land) project to protect endemic 
species.
o Promote environmental education and coastal clean-ups.
o Organize ecological courses on learning about local bio-diversity.
o Use our corporate influence to participate in environmental initiatives.

training and forest ecology environmental education.

Customer Services
	
Responsible Supply Chain
::: Appendixes
Customer approval is crucial to Compal’s success. We provide customers with the highest quality products and services, and maintain a 
positive partnership with our customers. Innovation and improvement is maintained from product design, R&D, manufacture to after-
sales service. All plants have obtained ISO 9001: 2015 international certification and introduced the QC 080000 hazardous substance 
management process with regular updates on the latest global environmental regulations and customers’ environmental standards. 
We constantly improve our quality management capability, work closely with customers, and continue to expect the highest quality 
standards from our supply chain to ensure that the quality policy is being properly enforced. There were no major quality incidents at 
Compal in 2023.

Responsible Supply Chain

08.1.1 Continued Innovation
Product Innovation
Compal is responding to rapid market changes and intensifying 
competition by continuing to partner with our customers 
on innovation and meeting new challenges. Continued 
development of our innovation and patenting abilities saw 
Compal collect 155 iF Design awards as of 2023. Our XR Cube 
(cloud service platform) product and APAL 5G MR Glasses also 
won the BC Category Award and Sustainable Tech Special Award 
at the 2023 COMPUTEX BC Awards. Our outstanding innovation 
ability is leveraged to co-develop critical technologies with the 
industry and innovative new products with our customers in 
order to continue supplying innovative products and services. 
At the same time, we also study our competitors, develop 
solutions, draw up product blueprints, and optimize product 
development processes in order to speed up time-to-market, as 
well as meet the customer launch schedule, expectations, and 
market demand.
B5G Satellite Internet-of-Things
The advanced MT6825 NTN chipset and LoRaWAN 
communication technology combines the advantages of 
IoT wide area communications technology and the two-way 
communication function of satellite networks to automatically 
link satellite signal with end sensor data. The result is a 
seamless communication experience for customers. Businesses 
can use satellite communication technology to implement 
connectivity and communications between IoT devices. The 
new technology roadmap at Compal now looks beyond 5G. 
Compal’s ESG energy management solution lets customers 
regulate their energy usage with absolute precision and embed 
imbue sustainability concepts in their business development, 
demonstrating Compal’s intelligent management of the Earth’s 
resources and commitment to energy efficiency.
Digital Supply Chain Management
Compal is actively working with customers to jointly promote 
the digital transformation of supply chain management. The 
introduction of Electronic Data Interchange (EDI) technology 
enables greater efficiency and digitization during customer 
ordering, supplier delivery and other processes. Total control 
over the production process can be achieved through precise 
analysis of data in the database. The distribution of customer 
orders can then be optimized while also reducing processing 
times and inactive stock risks during the production process, 
facilitating more efficient delivery of products and services to 
the customer.

8.1.2 Environmental 
Friendliness
8.1.3 Social 
Responsibility
8.1.4 Risk Control
Environmental and Energy Sustainability 
Compal has joined our customers in setting CDP 
targets such as Net Zero by 2050 and 100% renewable 
energy. We are also continuing to promote the ISO 
50001 certification system in order to improve energy 
efficiency and ratio of green energy. Compal is also 
actively cooperating with the GHG reduction targets of 
our customers. The Catalyze Program (carbon reduction 
plan for the semiconductor supply chain) is now 
being prioritized by customers so Compal will actively 
participate in and cooperate with the program too.
Performance and Certification
Corporate social responsibility is important to Compal. 
We strive to protect and improve our factory’s production 
environment and employee rights. We have obtained TCO 
factory certification for SA8000/RBA VAP as well as ISO 45001 
occupational health and safety management system and ISO 
14001 environmental management system certification to 
meet customer requirements on SER working hours. We have 
also passed multiple EcoVadis assessments to demonstrate 
Compal’s investment and accomplishments in sustainability.
Smart Healthcare Investment and Promotion
Compal is continuing to invest in smart healthcare and pitch it 
to our customers as well. The Smart Radio-frequency Ablation 
System (iRFA) co-developed with the Industrial Technology 
Research Institute made Compal the first domestic ICT vendor 
to partner with ITRI on advanced medical device technology. 
The technology has now received market approval in the US 
and Taiwan. Benefits include more precision for surgical safety 
and significant savings in operating time. A memorandum of 
understanding on MedTech investment was also signed with 
the Show Chwan Healthcare System in 2023 to focus on the 
development of surgical imaging solutions that will produce a 
world-class fusion of IT and healthcare.
Business Continuity Plan (BCP)
Geopolitical turmoil and the persistent impact of external 
factors means the ability to respond to supply chain changes 
is becoming increasingly important. Due to the unpredictable 
nature of the global supply chain, Compal is working actively 
promote a regionalized and distributed production presence 
based on target markets and customer requirements. Compal 
began accelerating our plant investment plants in Asia and 
Americas in 2018. In addition to increases in personnel and 
equipment, we also diversified the supply chain, strengthened 
corporate response ability, and reduced reliance on individual 
regions in order to lower risks, meet customer delivery 
requirements, and improve satisfaction.
Supply Chain Resilience
Compal is continuing to strengthen our supply chain resilience 
so that we can respond quickly to customer requirements, 
diversify risk, and meet customer delivery targets. Improving 
digital resilience, strengthening cyber security, and protecting 
customer privacy are also Compal initiatives on customer 
service. IoT technology is used to integrate manufacturing, 
warehousing, transportation, and sales to improve logistic 
efficiency; we have also developed strategic partnerships with 
suppliers to reduce risk from market changes and enhance our 
core corporate competitiveness.
